## User

Make a recommendation here (do not make any changes) on how to best organize files that serve as inputs and artifacts from Claude prompts. In general, I will create a prompt and possibly design documents, have you run the prompt to produce a specification and/or implementation plan, I will read and possibly hand-edit the specification/plan, I will prompt you to implement the feature using the specification/plan and possibly other files too, and at the end I will save a transcript of the Claude session together with some additional analytics/statistics files that I hand-create.  All these Claude session related files should be committed somewhere in the repo as a record of what I asked, discussions we had, and decisions that were made. These files will not be a primary source of documentation. You have permission to say "scrap that intention and do this instead." # Repo Organization Report: /workspace (pantheon-sitehealth-emails)

Git status is clean (working tree matches HEAD), so everything below reflects committed state. Everything is a single Python tool: one ~3,700-line script (`pantheon-sitehealth-emails`) plus plugin/check packages.

## 1. Top-level directory layout

Tracked source (committed):
- `pantheon-sitehealth-emails` — the main executable script (~162 KB, ~3,700 lines)
- `script_context.py` — shared-state module (imported as `sc`)
- `check/` — check-hook packages (`check/umich/sitelens.py`)
- `plugin/` — integration packages (`plugin/aws/get_secret.py`, `plugin/cloudflare/ips.py`, `plugin/umich/portal.py`)
- `docs/` — end-user docs (see #3)
- `prompts/` — canned Claude prompts (see #7)
- `email_template.html`, `email_template.txt`, `inline-styles.php`, `header-image.png` — rendering assets
- `sample-news/`, `news/` (`news/.gitkeep`) — news-item TOML inputs
- `sample-pantheon-sitehealth-emails.toml` — documented config template
- `pyproject.toml`, `uv.lock`, `composer.json`, `composer.lock`, `aws-config`, `monthly-report.txt`
- `README.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, `COPYRIGHT.txt`, `LICENSE.txt`
- `.claude/`, `.devcontainer/`, `.codegraph/.gitignore`, `.mcp.json`, `.gitignore`, `.envrc`

Generated / working data / not source (present on disk, mostly gitignored):
- `build/` — 1,580 entries; rendered per-site `.html`/`.txt`/`.eml` outputs (gitignored)
- `database.db` — 4.9 MB SQLite working DB (gitignored)
- `fqdns.json` — 148 KB generated cache (gitignored)
- `logs/` — 57 entries (note: NOT matched by `.gitignore`; see #2)
- `__pycache__/`, `.venv/`, `pantheon_sitehealth_emails.egg-info/`, `vendor/` — build/runtime artifacts
- `.idea/` — JetBrains IDE config
- `pantheon-sitehealth-emails-config/` — separate private repo checked out here (see #5)
- Symlinks: `pantheon-sitehealth-emails.toml`, `local.toml` (see #5)

## 2. `.gitignore` (verbatim)

File: `/workspace/.gitignore`

```

/pantheon-sitehealth-emails-config

[... standard editor/backup patterns ...]

# macOS stuff
[.DS_Store etc.]

# Logs
[log patterns]

# Python stuff
[__pycache__, .venv, egg-info etc.]

# PHP stuff
[vendor/ etc.]

# don't commit composer.lock since different people may be using
# different versions of PHP, which in turn cause differences in
# composer package dependencies
# (composer.lock — note: it IS actually tracked despite this comment)

# dotenv environment variables files
.env*
```

Key observations for your artifact convention:
- Build/generated data is explicitly ignored: `/build/`, `/database.db`, `/fqdns.json`, `/site_results.json`, `*-results.json`, `*.csv`, `/tmp/`.
- No pattern for `.eml`, `.html`, or `.txt` outputs — they live inside the already-ignored `/build/` dir, so they're covered by location, not extension. CLAUDE.md confirms: "`database.db`, `fqdns.json`, and the `.eml`/`.html`/`.txt` outputs are working data, not source."
- No `transcripts`, `sessions`, `.claude/`-artifact, or AI-output patterns exist yet.
- `.env*` is ignored (dotenv secrets).
- The whole private config dir `/pantheon-sitehealth-emails-config` and its symlinks are ignored.
- There is a "Logs" section, but the top-level `logs/` directory is present on disk and appears not fully covered — worth noting if session logs would land there.

## 3. Existing docs / decisions / notes directories

- Only `docs/` exists. No `decisions/`, `adr/`, `notes/`, `sessions/`, or `ai/` anywhere.
- `docs/` contents (both tracked):
  - `/workspace/docs/aws-credentials.md` (3.4 KB)
  - `/workspace/docs/awscli-login.md` (1.1 KB)
- Per the canned prompt convention (see #7), `docs/` is explicitly reserved for **end-user documentation only**: "do not document internal functioning of the program in docs/, only end-user instructions."
- Other markdown design/spec docs: none currently. `README.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, `.claude/CLAUDE.md`, the two `prompts/*.md`, and the config repo's `README.md` are the only markdown files. The `new-feature-design` prompt references writing a `./SPEC.md` at repo root, but no `SPEC.md` currently exists.

## 4. README.md TODO list ("TO DO" section, verbatim)

```
## TO DO

* set up devcontainer
  * make sure script works on its own
    * Terminus machine token (filesystem for now, AWS Secrets Manager later?)
    * SSH and key (ssh-agent for now, something else later?)
    * UMich Kerberos password --&gt; replace with SendGrid API key in AWS Secrets Manager
    * Cloudflare credentials (special read-only token from AWS Secrets Manager?)
    * AWS credentials (set in environment for now)
* test harness
* test suite
* rework everything from ~3,700 line script into a combination of plugins and other Python files/packages
* have Claude document plugin system and config file
* update CLAUDE.md again (prompt)
* add SendGrid support as an additional option to SMTP
* fqdns.json (get direct from Cloudflare instead; refresh if --all or multiple sites and &gt;= 24h)
* add cf-cache-status, cache-control checks
* switch to Pantheon API where possible?
* add everything to its-webhosting/terraform-infra repo

* Switch terminus() to returning tuple (output, errors, fatal) for better error handling

* Check Live environment (not Dev) for the version of PHP, Drupal/WordPress, and all the
  plugins/modules/themes and if everything is up to date there then skip asking Pantheon
  about updates pending in the Dev environment. This way, site owners that are not using
  the Pantheon WebOps workflow won't be getting wrong information.

* Report on environment lock (no notice, just a report section)

* Send daily traffic alerts
  * A comparison of the site's month-to-date visits count compared to a prorated version
    of that site's monthly limit. If they are at or below zero at any point in the month,
    flag for extra visibility.
  * A comparison of the previous day's visits to the visits from the day before that. If
    the percentage increase is high AND the visits count is high enough, flag for extra
    visibility. This number is a bit less useful, as a very low-traffic site can see a
    200-300% increase from day-to-day that is effectively meaningless (e.g. 60 visits
    instead of 20).
  * Monthly visits remaining on a prorated limit basis, calculated by the current day of the month
  * Query Cloudflare for a fuller traffic picture

* Move nightly traffic capture into portal app

* Add a notice for accessibility scores below a certain number given to us by the
  accessibility team.

* Measure PHP memory usage and factor that into plan recommendations

* Add % of traffic cached by _Cloudflare_ to traffic table (to show/maximize cost savings)

* Add security score to SiteLens. Include Cloudflare Radar, SSL Labs,
  securityheaders.com / Mozilla Observatory API, pending updates, best practices, check
  internals of site (filesystem config, ...)

* Add a Cloudflare score to SiteLens: DNS, cache headers for pages/assets/api, check
  internals (SSL Full/Strict, WAF not disabled, ...)

* Attach data as CSV

* See if we can get a better recommendation by using AI -- either a customized LLM, or a
  specifically trained DNN
```

## 5. The "separate private config repo" pattern

This is a strong, load-bearing convention in the repo:

- `pantheon-sitehealth-emails-config/` is a **separate private git repo checked out inside `/workspace`** — it has its own nested `.git` directory (confirmed: "HAS .git (nested repo)"). Contents: its own `README.md`, `news/`, and the real `pantheon-sitehealth-emails.toml` (4 KB).
- The active config is a **symlink**: `/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails.toml -&gt; pantheon-sitehealth-emails-config/pantheon-sitehealth-emails.toml` (created Feb 2025).
- A second symlink `/workspace/local.toml -&gt; sample-pantheon-sitehealth-emails.toml` points at the public template.
- Both the symlink target dir and the symlink itself are gitignored:
  ```
  /pantheon-sitehealth-emails.toml
  /pantheon-sitehealth-emails-config
  /local.toml
  ```
- README setup instructions codify it: `git clone git@github.com:its-webhosting/pantheon-sitehealth-emails-config.git # private repo` then `ln -s pantheon-sitehealth-emails-config/pantheon-sitehealth-emails.toml .`
- CLAUDE.md reinforces the separation-of-concerns intent: institution-specific data (plan names, prices, org id, DB, Cloudflare/AWS toggles) lives in the private config repo, and "Keep U-M-only logic out of the core script and behind config flags / `umich` plugin+check packages so the tool stays reusable by other institutions."

Takeaway: the user already has an established pattern of keeping institution-private/sensitive material in a separate gitignored repo, symlinked into the main tree.

## 6. Secrets handling

From CLAUDE.md ("Required runtime credentials / external tools") and the README TODO, secrets currently come from the runtime environment / local filesystem, not from committed files:

- `SMTP_PASSWORD` — U-M Kerberos password for `smtp.mail.umich.edu:465`, read from the environment, referenced in `smtp_login()`.
- Pantheon machine token — held by an authenticated `terminus` on the filesystem (`.devcontainer/terminus/cache/tokens/**`, gitignored).
- Pantheon SSH key — loaded into `ssh-agent` (`.devcontainer/ssh/keys/**`, gitignored).
- `AWS_*` (`AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID`/`AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY` or an `aws configure --profile webhosting`) and `CLOUDFLARE_EMAIL` / `CLOUDFLARE_API_KEY` — from the environment.
- `.env*` is gitignored.
- There is an `aws-config` file and `docs/aws-credentials.md` / `docs/awscli-login.md` for AWS login guidance.
- CLAUDE.md notes: "Secret handling here is still a work in progress (see README TODO)" — the TODO plans to migrate tokens/passwords to AWS Secrets Manager and replace the Kerberos SMTP password with a SendGrid API key.

Risk note for your assessment: because live secrets flow through the process environment (and `SMTP_PASSWORD` is described as "hardcoded in `smtp_login()`" at runtime via env), raw session transcripts or command-output captures could plausibly contain credential values (env dumps, `terminus` auth output, AWS CLI output). There is currently no gitignore rule that would catch a committed transcript.

## 7. `.claude/` directory and canned prompts

`.claude/` at repo root (all tracked):
- `/workspace/.claude/CLAUDE.md` — contains a "CodeGraph" usage section (guidance to prefer `codegraph_explore`; ends with `&lt;!-- CODEGRAPH_END --&gt;`).
- `/workspace/.claude/settings.json`
- `/workspace/.claude/settings.local.json`

No `.claude/commands/` or prompt files live under `.claude/`. The "canned prompts" from the recent commit live in a **top-level `prompts/` directory** instead:

- `/workspace/prompts/new-feature-design.prompt-template.md` (9.9 KB) — a structured feature-design prompt template. Sections: **Task**, **Steps to Perform / Methodology**, **Prime Directives**, **Engineering Preferences**, **Quality control**, **Adversarial Review**. Notably it instructs the model to "Write the complete specifications ... to the file `./SPEC.md`, optimized for Claude Code to use it to implement the code" and states SPEC.md "will also serve as a record for both Claude Code and humans for what was decided and why, but it will not be a primary source of documentation." It also says end-user docs go in `docs/` (end-user instructions only, not internal functioning), and CLAUDE.md should capture "things that you can't easily learn by looking at the code."
- `/workspace/prompts/update-claude-md.md` (1.7 KB) — a prompt ("Prompt: update the CLAUDE.md file") for regenerating/refreshing CLAUDE.md after changes.

Relevant existing conventions this reveals for your session-artifact decision: the repo already distinguishes (a) `prompts/` for reusable prompt templates, (b) a planned root-level `SPEC.md` for per-feature design/decision records described as a human+Claude record but "not a primary source of documentation," (c) `docs/` strictly for end-user docs, and (d) CLAUDE.md for non-obvious internal knowledge. `.mcp.json`, `.codegraph/`, and `.claude/settings*.json` configure the AI tooling. No location is yet designated for transcripts, generated specs beyond `SPEC.md`, or analytics files.</result>

## Assistant

That exploration is gold — it turns out you already have most of a convention half-built, and it surfaces a real risk you may not have weighed. Let me reflect what I found and then dig into the hard forks.

**What already exists (relevant to this):**
- `prompts/` holds reusable prompt *templates* (`new-feature-design.prompt-template.md`, `update-claude-md.md`).
- That feature-design template already tells Claude to write `./SPEC.md` **at repo root** — described in almost your exact words: *"a record for both Claude Code and humans for what was decided and why, but not a primary source of documentation."* But it's a **single fixed path** — every feature would overwrite the last. So there's no accumulating record today. That's the gap you're really filling.
- `docs/` is reserved strictly for end-user docs; CLAUDE.md for non-obvious internals.
- You have a strong established pattern: **institution-private/sensitive material lives in a separate gitignored repo** (`pantheon-sitehealth-emails-config`), symlinked in.
- `.gitignore` excludes generated data by *location* (`build/`, `database.db`, etc.). **There is no rule that would catch a committed transcript.**

**Two things I want to flag before you answer:**
1. **This tool is explicitly meant to be reusable by other institutions.** Your internal AI-development transcripts are U-M process noise to a downstream cloner — an argument for *not* putting them in the main tree.
2. **Secrets leak risk.** Your live secrets (`SMTP_PASSWORD`, machine token, AWS/Cloudflare keys) flow through the environment and command output. Raw transcripts can capture env dumps, `terminus` auth output, AWS CLI output — and nothing in `.gitignore` would stop you committing them.

Here are the forks that actually change the recommendation:

## Assistant

{
  "file_path": "/home/node/.claude/plans/make-a-recommendation-here-keen-gadget.md",
  "content": "# Convention for Claude session artifacts (`sessions/`)\n\n## Context\n\nMark's workflow for building features with Claude follows a repeatable cycle:\ncreate a prompt (+ optional design docs) → Claude produces a spec/implementation\nplan → Mark reads and hand-edits it → Mark prompts Claude to implement using the\nspec → at the end Mark saves a session transcript plus hand-created\nanalytics/statistics files. He wants all of these committed **as a historical\nrecord** of what was asked, what was discussed, and what was decided — explicitly\n**not** as a primary source of documentation.\n\nToday there is no home for this. The repo already has adjacent pieces:\n`prompts/` holds reusable prompt *templates*; `new-feature-design.prompt-template.md`\nalready tells Claude to write a spec — but to a **single fixed `./SPEC.md` at repo\nroot**, which every feature would overwrite, so nothing accumulates. `docs/` is\nreserved for end-user docs; CLAUDE.md is for non-obvious internals. This plan adds\nthe missing accumulating archive and reconciles the existing template with it.\n\nTwo risks shaped the design: (1) the tool is meant to be reusable by other\ninstitutions, so U-M's dev history is noise to downstream cloners; (2) live secrets\n(`SMTP_PASSWORD`, Pantheon machine token, `AWS_*`, `CLOUDFLARE_*`) flow through the\nenvironment and command output, so raw transcripts can leak credentials — and\nnothing in `.gitignore` currently catches a committed transcript.\n\n## Decisions (from the interview)\n\n- **Location:** a committed top-level `sessions/` directory in **this** repo.\n- **Grouping:** one folder per feature/task cycle, named `YYYY-MM-DD-slug`, sorting\n  chronologically. Multiple prompts/sessions for one feature nest inside it.\n- **Transcripts:** scrub secrets, then commit the scrubbed version; keep raw exports\n  gitignored.\n- **Commit coupling:** the session folder lands in the **same commit** as the\n  implementation, so code and its rationale are atomic.\n- **Three defaults chosen on Mark's behalf while he was away (all easily reversible):**\n  spec is written **directly into the session folder** (template updated) rather\n  than at root-then-moved; scrub gets **both** a helper script **and** a manual\n  checklist; the transcript source is the **Claude Code session JSONL**\n  (`~/.claude/projects/.../*.jsonl`), converted to markdown and scrubbed.\n\n## Target structure\n\n```\nsessions/\n  README.md                         # the convention itself (see below)\n  scrub-transcript.py               # JSONL -> scrubbed markdown transcript\n  2026-07-03-daily-traffic-alerts/\n    01-design.prompt.md             # input: the design prompt used\n    design-notes/                   # input: optional hand-authored design docs\n    SPEC.md                         # generated spec/plan, then hand-edited\n    02-implement.prompt.md          # input: the implementation prompt used\n    transcript.md                   # scrubbed session transcript(s)\n    analytics.md                    # hand-created stats/analytics\n  2026-07-20-sitelens-security-score/\n    ...\n```\n\nConventions inside a feature folder:\n- **Ordering:** numeric prefixes (`01-`, `02-`, …) on prompt files reflect the order\n  they were used across the cycle. Non-ordered artifacts (`SPEC.md`, `transcript.md`,\n  `analytics.md`) use canonical fixed names.\n- **Multiple sessions:** if a feature spans several sessions, use\n  `transcript-01.md`, `transcript-02.md`, … (single session stays `transcript.md`).\n- **Slug:** short kebab-case; prefer matching the README TODO wording when the work\n  maps to a TODO item, so the archive is easy to cross-reference.\n\n## Files to create / modify\n\n1. **`sessions/README.md` (new)** — the authoritative statement of this convention:\n   folder naming, the canonical file list and their roles, the end-to-end workflow\n   steps, the \"record, not documentation\" caveat, the same-commit rule, and the\n   **secret-scrub checklist** (grep for `SMTP_PASSWORD`, `AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID`,\n   `AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY`, `CLOUDFLARE_API_KEY`, `CLOUDFLARE_EMAIL`, `machine_token`,\n   `session`, `Bearer `, SSH key blocks before committing).\n\n2. **`sessions/scrub-transcript.py` (new)** — small standalone script (match the\n   repo's plain-Python style; no new deps). Input: a Claude Code session JSONL path\n   (default: newest under `~/.claude/projects/-workspace/`). Output: a readable\n   markdown `transcript.md` with secrets **redacted**. Redaction covers: values of\n   the known secret env vars above, `Bearer <token>` / `Authorization` headers,\n   Pantheon `machine_token`/`session` JSON fields, AWS access-key/secret shapes\n   (`AKIA…`, 40-char secrets), and `-----BEGIN … PRIVATE KEY-----` blocks. Writes the\n   unredacted intermediate as `*.raw.md` (gitignored). Redaction is best-effort — the\n   manual checklist in the README is the backstop.\n\n3. **`.gitignore` (modify)** — add a safety net so raw/unscrubbed exports can never be\n   committed by accident, while scrubbed artifacts are tracked. Add (near the existing\n   working-data patterns):\n   ```\n   # Claude session archive: keep scrubbed artifacts, never raw exports\n   /sessions/**/*.raw.md\n   /sessions/**/*.raw.jsonl\n   ```\n\n4. **`prompts/new-feature-design.prompt-template.md` (modify)** — change the spec\n   target from `./SPEC.md` to `sessions/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/SPEC.md`, instructing the\n   run to create the dated feature folder first and write the spec into it. Preserve\n   the existing \"record for humans and Claude, not a primary source of documentation\"\n   language. Leave the rest of the template (methodology, prime directives,\n   adversarial review) untouched.\n\n5. **`CLAUDE.md` (modify, root project file)** — add a short subsection (under\n   \"Conventions & gotchas\" or a new \"Session artifacts\" heading) pointing to\n   `sessions/README.md`: what the archive is, the `YYYY-MM-DD-slug` folder rule, that\n   it's a historical record and **not** documentation, that transcripts must be\n   scrubbed before commit, and that the folder is committed atomically with the code.\n   Keep it to a few lines — the detail lives in `sessions/README.md`.\n\n## Reuse / alignment notes\n\n- Mirrors the existing `prompts/` (inputs) vs. new `sessions/` (per-run record)\n  split, and the repo's habit of ignoring bulky/sensitive data by location.\n- Supersedes the root-level single `./SPEC.md` in the current template — the reason\n  that path exists (a decision record) is exactly what `sessions/<feature>/SPEC.md`\n  now provides, per-feature and accumulating.\n- Deliberately **not** a separate/nested repo (that option was considered for the\n  reusability/secrets reasons but declined in favor of keeping the record in-tree);\n  the scrub step + gitignore net are what make the in-tree choice safe.\n\n## Verification\n\n1. **Structure & sort:** create `sessions/` with two dated folders and confirm\n   `ls sessions/` sorts chronologically.\n2. **Scrub works:** run `python sessions/scrub-transcript.py` against a real session\n   JSONL that contains tool output; confirm the produced `transcript.md` has known\n   secrets redacted — `grep -E 'SMTP_PASSWORD|AKIA|BEGIN [A-Z ]*PRIVATE KEY|Bearer '\n   sessions/**/transcript.md` returns nothing — while the `*.raw.md` intermediate\n   still has them.\n3. **Gitignore net:** `git check-ignore sessions/x/transcript.raw.md` (and `.raw.jsonl`)\n   report ignored; `git status` shows `transcript.md`, `SPEC.md`, prompts, and\n   `analytics.md` as trackable.\n4. **Template dry-run:** read `prompts/new-feature-design.prompt-template.md` and\n   confirm it now directs output into `sessions/<date-slug>/SPEC.md` and instructs\n   creating the folder first.\n5. **End-to-end:** on the next real feature, run the full cycle into a dated folder\n   and confirm the whole record (prompts + spec + scrubbed transcript + analytics)\n   commits atomically with the implementation.\n"
}

## Assistant

Good — those three are settled except the transcript source, which you rightly want to actually talk through rather than have me assume. Here's the real tradeoff.

**What you commit today:** `/export path/transcript.txt` gives a human-readable rendering — the right artifact for "a record humans read," which is exactly your stated purpose ("not a primary source of documentation"). I'd keep that as the committed `transcript.md`.

**What committing the session JSONL would add:**
- **Fidelity** — the JSONL is the complete structured log: every tool call, full (untruncated) tool output, timestamps, model, and **token/cost usage**. `/export` is a lossy human view of that.
- **Analytics as data, not prose** — you hand-create analytics/statistics files. The JSONL is literally the source data for those numbers (token counts, tool-use counts, durations, cost). Committing it makes those stats **reproducible and auditable** later, instead of trusting a hand-typed number.
- **Future re-processing** — you could re-render or re-analyze a session with better tooling down the road.

**What it costs:**
- **Bulkier and noisier** — bloats the tree with a machine format nobody reads.
- **More secret exposure** — the JSONL carries *raw* tool outputs (terminus auth, env dumps, AWS/Cloudflare CLI output), i.e. *more* credentials than the already-rendered `/export` text, and JSON is fiddlier to scrub reliably than flat text.
- **Redundant** for the human-record purpose — the `/export` text already covers that.

**My read:** the `/export` transcript is the right *committed record*. The JSONL's real value is as the *data behind your analytics files* — and once you've written those numbers down, that value is largely banked. So I lean toward: commit the scrubbed text transcript; keep the JSONL locally (gitignored) as the optional data source when you want to compute/verify analytics, and only commit a scrubbed JSONL for a specific session if reproducible analytics genuinely matter there. One question to pin it:

### ⚙ Tool call: `AskUserQuestion`

```json
{
  "questions": [
    {
      "question": "Given that tradeoff, how should the session JSONL be treated relative to the /export text transcript you already commit?",
      "header": "JSONL policy",
      "multiSelect": false,
      "options": [
        {
          "label": "Text only; JSONL local (Recommended)",
          "description": "Commit the scrubbed /export transcript as the record. Keep the JSONL locally but gitignored, documented as the optional data source you can run analytics against. Cleanest tree; JSONL fidelity available when you want it, never shipped.",
          "preview": "committed:  transcript.md   (scrubbed /export text)\n            analytics.md    (hand-created)\nlocal only: *.jsonl          (gitignored data source\n                              for computing analytics)"
        },
        {
          "label": "Commit text + scrubbed JSONL",
          "description": "Always commit both the scrubbed text transcript AND a scrubbed JSONL, for full fidelity and reproducible analytics on every feature. Cost: bulkier tree and a heavier, riskier scrub step on the raw JSON every time.",
          "preview": "committed:  transcript.md   (scrubbed /export text)\n            session.jsonl   (scrubbed full log)\n            analytics.md"
        },
        {
          "label": "Text always; JSONL when useful",
          "description": "Commit the text transcript every time; commit a scrubbed JSONL only for sessions where reproducible/auditable analytics genuinely matter. Flexible, but the rule is judgment-based rather than uniform.",

## Assistant

Excellent — that reframes the JSONL nicely: don't commit it, **mine it**. The JSONL becomes the local data source that the finalize script reads to emit a human-readable statistics file into the session folder. That resolves the last fork. Let me update the plan to reflect all your decisions, including one honesty caveat you should know about up front.

**Caveat I need to flag:** `/usage`, `/context`, `/ctx-stats`, and `rtk gain` aren't uniformly script-accessible:
- **Per-session token/cost usage** (like `/usage`) — cleanly derivable from the JSONL; every assistant turn records input/output/cache token counts. Solid.
- **Context-window breakdown** (like `/context`) — a live-session snapshot; from the JSONL after the fact I can only *approximate* it (final-context token totals by role/tool), not reproduce the exact live view.
- **`rtk gain`** — the script can shell out to `rtk gain` and capture its output *if* `rtk` is on PATH; note its numbers are cumulative, not strictly this-session-scoped.
- **`/ctx-stats`** — that's a context-mode slash command backed by an MCP tool, not obviously invocable from a plain script. I'll need to find whether context-mode exposes a non-interactive path; if not, that section falls back to a documented manual paste.

I'll build what's cleanly derivable, shell out where a CLI exists, and mark the approximate/uncertain sources so we verify each during implementation rather than pretending they're all one clean `--json` call.

## Assistant

Got it — that's a meaningful architecture upgrade, and a good one. The orchestrator becomes a **manually-invoked Claude skill**, which actually *solves* the two problems I flagged earlier: because the skill runs inside the live session, it can call context-mode's `ctx_stats` MCP tool directly (no more "can't get `/ctx-stats` from a script") and run `rtk gain` via Bash, then hand those to the deterministic script for assembly. One design stance I'm baking in: **secret-scrubbing stays as deterministic regex in the Python script, not LLM judgment** — you don't want a model "mostly" redacting a credential. The skill orchestrates and supplies the in-session data; the script does the reliable, testable, redaction + stats assembly.

Because it\nruns *in* the live session, it can reach tools the script can't. Steps:\n1. Determine/confirm the target `sessions/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/` folder (argument, or infer\n   from the active SPEC/branch, or prompt).\n2. Capture in-session-only data to gitignored `*.raw.txt` files: run `rtk gain` via\n   Bash (if `rtk` on PATH); call the context-mode `ctx_stats` MCP tool (if configured).\n4. The plan is complete and reflects everything we settled: the `sessions/` archive, per-feature `YYYY-MM-DD-slug` folders, spec written straight into the folder, `/export`-based scrubbed transcripts (JSONL mined but never committed), the deterministic `finalize-session.py` for scrubbing + stats, and the manually-invoked `/archive-session` skill that orchestrates it all before you ask Claude to commit.

### ⚙ Tool call: `ExitPlanMode`

```json
{
  "plan": "# Convention + tooling for Claude session artifacts (`sessions/` + `/archive-session` skill)\n\n## Context\n\nMark builds features with Claude in a repeatable cycle: write a prompt (+ optional\ndesign docs) → Claude produces a spec/implementation plan → Mark reads and hand-edits\nit → Mark prompts Claude to implement using the spec → at session end, capture a\ntranscript plus statistics/analytics. He wants all of it committed **as a historical\nrecord** of what was asked, discussed, and decided — explicitly **not** a primary\nsource of documentation.\n\nToday there's no home for this. Adjacent pieces exist: `prompts/` holds reusable\nprompt *templates*; `new-feature-design.prompt-template.md` already writes a spec —\nbut to a single fixed `./SPEC.md` at repo root that every feature overwrites, so\nnothing accumulates. `docs/` is end-user docs only; CLAUDE.md is non-obvious\ninternals. This plan adds the accumulating archive, the tooling to populate it, and a\nmanually-invoked skill to orchestrate the end-of-session capture.\n\nTwo risks shaped it: (1) the tool is meant to be reusable by other institutions, so\nU-M dev history is noise to downstream cloners; (2) live secrets (`SMTP_PASSWORD`,\nPantheon machine token, `AWS_*`, `CLOUDFLARE_*`) flow through the environment and\ncommand output, so raw transcripts/logs can leak credentials — and `.gitignore`\ncatches none of that today.\n\n## Decisions (from the interview)\n\n- **Location:** committed top-level `sessions/` directory in **this** repo.\n- **Grouping:** one folder per feature/task cycle, `YYYY-MM-DD-slug`, chronologically\n  sortable. Multiple prompts/sessions for one feature nest inside it.\n- **Spec:** session folder is created first; the spec is written **directly** into it\n  (`sessions/<date-slug>/SPEC.md`); the design prompt template is updated to target\n  that path. No root `SPEC.md`, no move step.\n- **Transcript source:** the human-readable output of `/export` (a `.txt`), which Mark\n  already produces — the committed record. The raw session JSONL is **not committed**;\n  it's mined locally for statistics and is gitignored.\n- **Secret handling:** deterministic regex scrubbing in a Python script (not LLM\n  judgment), plus a `.gitignore` safety net so raw exports and JSONL logs can never be\n  committed by accident.\n- **Statistics:** auto-generated into `statistics.md` from the JSONL + in-session data\n  (see spec below): usage, context-window (approx), rtk gain, ctx-stats, session\n  metadata, cost estimate.\n- **Orchestration:** a manually-invoked Claude skill (`/archive-session`) that, at\n  session end, gathers the in-session-only data, runs the script, and writes the\n  artifacts into the session folder. Slug prefers matching README TODO wording when applicable.\n\n## Component 1 — `sessions/finalize-session.py` (deterministic core)\n\nPlain-Python house style, no new deps, runnable standalone (so it's testable outside a\nsession). Two jobs:\n\n**A. Scrub the transcript.** Input: `/export` text (`transcript.raw.txt`). Output:\n`transcript.md`, secrets redacted via regex — values of `SMTP_PASSWORD`,\n`AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID`/`AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY` (incl. `AKIA…` / 40-char secret shapes),\n`CLOUDFLARE_API_KEY`/`CLOUDFLARE_EMAIL`, Pantheon `machine_token`/`session`,\n`Bearer <token>` / `Authorization` headers, `-----BEGIN … PRIVATE KEY-----` blocks.\nBest-effort; README documents a manual grep backstop before commit.\n\n**B. Assemble `statistics.md`** from the session JSONL\n(`~/.claude/projects/-workspace/*.jsonl`, newest by default; overridable) plus\nskill-supplied capture files (below). Sections, each nicely formatted:\n- **Session metadata:** date/time, duration, model(s) used, turn count, tool-call\n  counts by tool. *(From JSONL — reliable.)*\n- **Usage** (like `/usage`): per-model input / output / cache-read / cache-write token\n  totals, aggregated from each assistant turn's `usage` block. *(From JSONL —\n  reliable, primary section.)*\n- **Cost estimate:** prefer any per-message cost field present in the JSONL; else\n  compute tokens × a maintained per-model price table. **Pricing source/table must be\n  chosen and kept current during implementation** (models/prices change) — flag it.\n- **Context window** (like `/context`): best-effort reconstruction of final context\n  size by role/tool, **labeled as an approximation** (the exact live `/context` view\n  can't be reproduced post-hoc).\n- **rtk gain:** embed the skill-captured `rtk gain` output if present; note it's\n  cumulative, not strictly per-session. ## Assistant

Right — and that's fully achievable, with one clean consequence worth stating. Claude can't invoke `/export` programmatically (it's a built-in CLI command the user types), but it doesn't need to: the session JSONL we're already mining for statistics contains the entire conversation, so the script can **render the transcript directly from the JSONL** and scrub it. That removes the manual `/export` step entirely — you invoke one skill and everything is produced.

The only trade-off: `transcript.md` becomes our own JSONL→markdown rendering rather than Claude Code's official `/export` formatting. Given you want single-invocation automation, that's the right call. Let me fix the plan accordingly.

  "new_string": "- **Transcript source:** the skill renders the committed `transcript.md` **directly\n  from the session JSONL** (`~/.claude/projects/-workspace/*.jsonl`) — no manual\n  `/export` step; one skill invocation does everything. Trade-off accepted: this is our own\n  JSONL→markdown rendering, not Claude Code's official `/export` format, in exchange for\n  full one-command automation."

Multiple prompts/sessions for one feature nest inside it.\n- **Spec:** session folder is created first; the spec is written **directly** into it\n  (`sessions/<date-slug>/SPEC.md`); the design prompt template is updated to target\n  that path. No root `SPEC.md`, no move step.\n- **Transcript source:** the skill renders the committed `transcript.md` **directly\n  from the session JSONL** (`~/.claude/projects/-workspace/*.jsonl`) — no manual\n  `/export` step; one skill invocation does everything. The JSONL itself is mined for\n  statistics but is **not committed** (gitignored). Trade-off accepted: this is our own\n  JSONL→markdown rendering, not Claude Code's official `/export` format, in exchange for\n  full one-command automation.\n- **Secret handling:** deterministic regex scrubbing in a Python script (not LLM\n  judgment), plus a `.gitignore` safety net so raw exports and JSONL logs can never be\n  committed by accident.\n- **Statistics:** auto-generated into `statistics.md` from the JSONL + in-session data\n  (see spec below): usage, context-window (approx), rtk gain, ctx-stats, session\n  metadata, cost estimate.\n- **Orchestration:** a manually-invoked Claude skill (`/archive-session`) that, at\n  session end, gathers the in-session-only data, runs the script, and writes the\n  artifacts into the session folder. Mark then asks Claude to commit everything (Claude\n  writes the commit message).\n- **Commit coupling:** the session folder lands in the **same commit** as the\n  implementation.\n\n## Target structure\n\n```\n.claude/skills/archive-session/SKILL.md   # manually-invoked orchestrator skill\nsessions/\n  README.md                               # the convention itself\n  finalize-session.py                     # deterministic scrub + stats assembly\n  2026-07-03-daily-traffic-alerts/\n    01-design.prompt.md                   # input: design prompt used\n    design-notes/                         # input: optional hand-authored design docs\n    SPEC.md                               # generated spec/plan, then hand-edited\n    02-implement.prompt.md                # input: implementation prompt used\n    transcript.md                         # scrubbed /export transcript (committed)\n    statistics.md                         # auto-generated session stats (committed)\n    analytics.md                          # optional hand-written analysis (scaffolded)\n  2026-07-20-sitelens-security-score/\n    ...\n```\n\nInside a feature folder: numeric prefixes (`01-`, `02-`) order prompt files; fixed\nnames for `SPEC.md`/`transcript.md`/`statistics.md`/`analytics.md`; multi-session work\nuses `transcript-01.md`/`statistics-01.md`, etc. `statistics.md` is machine-generated\n(don't hand-edit); `analytics.md` is Mark's narrative (skill scaffolds an empty\ntemplate). Slug prefers matching README TODO wording when applicable.\n\n## Component 1 — `sessions/finalize-session.py` (deterministic core)\n\nPlain-Python house style, no new deps, runnable standalone (so it's testable outside a\nsession). Two jobs:\n\n**A. Render + scrub the transcript.** Read the session JSONL and render it to readable\nmarkdown (user/assistant turns, tool calls, tool results, thinking blocks), writing the\nunscrubbed intermediate as `transcript.raw.md` (gitignored). Then produce\n`transcript.md` with secrets redacted via regex — values of `SMTP_PASSWORD`,\n`AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID`/`AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY` (incl. `AKIA…` / 40-char secret shapes),\n`CLOUDFLARE_API_KEY`/`CLOUDFLARE_EMAIL`, Pantheon `machine_token`/`session`,\n`Bearer <token>` / `Authorization` headers, `-----BEGIN … PRIVATE KEY-----` blocks.\nBest-effort; README documents a manual grep backstop before commit. (May optionally\naccept a pre-run `/export` text as an override input for higher-fidelity formatting.)\n\n**B. Assemble `statistics.md`** from the session JSONL\n(`~/.claude/projects/-workspace/*.jsonl`, newest by default; overridable) plus\nskill-supplied capture files (below). Sections, each nicely formatted:\n- **Session metadata:** date/time, duration, model(s) used, turn count, tool-call\n  counts by tool. *(From JSONL — reliable.)*\n- **Usage** (like `/usage`): per-model input / output / cache-read / cache-write token\n  totals, aggregated from each assistant turn's `usage` block. *(From JSONL —\n  reliable, primary section.)*\n- **Cost estimate:** prefer any per-message cost field present in the JSONL; else\n  compute tokens × a maintained per-model price table. **Pricing source/table must be\n  chosen and kept current during implementation** (models/prices change) — flag it.\n- **Context window** (like `/context`): best-effort reconstruction of final context\n  size by role/tool, **labeled as an approximation** (the exact live `/context` view\n  can't be reproduced post-hoc).\n- **rtk gain:** embed the skill-captured `rtk gain` output if present; note it's\n  cumulative, not strictly per-session. Omit cleanly if absent.\n- **context-mode** (like `/ctx-stats`): embed the skill-captured `ctx_stats` output if\n  present. Omit cleanly if absent.\n\nThe script degrades gracefully: any missing input → section omitted, never a crash.\n\n## Component 2 — `.claude/skills/archive-session/SKILL.md` (orchestrator)\n\nA project skill Mark invokes manually at session end (`/archive-session`). Because it\nruns *in* the live session, it can reach tools the script can't. Steps:\n1. Determine/confirm the target `sessions/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/` folder (argument, or infer\n   from the active SPEC/branch, or prompt).\n2. Capture in-session-only data to gitignored `*.raw.txt` files: run `rtk gain` via\n   Bash (if `rtk` on PATH); call the context-mode `ctx_stats` MCP tool (if configured).\n3. Run `finalize-session.py`, passing the folder + capture files → it renders + scrubs\n   `transcript.md` from the newest session JSONL and assembles `statistics.md`.\n4. Scaffold an empty `analytics.md` template for Mark's narrative (if absent).\n5. Report what was written; do **not** commit. Mark then asks Claude to commit\n   everything (Claude writes the commit message).\n\nRationale for the script/skill split: scrubbing and number-crunching stay deterministic\nand testable in Python (never trust an LLM to reliably redact a credential or format\ntoken math); the skill only does what genuinely needs the live session (capturing\n`ctx_stats`/`rtk gain`, wiring paths, scaffolding). No git pre-commit hook — the skill\nis per-session, invoked on demand.\n\n## Other files to create / modify\n\n- **`sessions/README.md` (new)** — authoritative convention: folder naming, canonical\n  files/roles, end-to-end workflow (below), \"record, not documentation\" caveat,\n  same-commit rule, how `/archive-session` and `finalize-session.py` fit together, and\n  the manual secret-review grep.\n- **`.gitignore` (modify)** — add near the working-data patterns:\n  ```\n  # Claude session archive: keep scrubbed artifacts, never raw exports or logs\n  /sessions/**/*.raw.txt\n  /sessions/**/*.raw.md\n  /sessions/**/*.jsonl\n  ```\n- **`prompts/new-feature-design.prompt-template.md` (modify)** — retarget the spec from\n  `./SPEC.md` to `sessions/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/SPEC.md`, instructing the run to create the\n  dated folder first. Preserve the \"record for humans and Claude, not primary\n  documentation\" language; leave other sections untouched.\n- **`CLAUDE.md` (modify, root)** — short \"Session artifacts\" subsection pointing to\n  `sessions/README.md`: what the archive is, the `YYYY-MM-DD-slug` rule, that it's a\n  record and **not** documentation, that transcripts are scrubbed via `/archive-session`\n  before commit, that the JSONL is never committed, and that the folder commits\n  atomically with the code.\n\n## End-to-end workflow (documented in `sessions/README.md`)\n\n1. Start a feature: create `sessions/<date-slug>/`, drop the design prompt in as\n   `01-design.prompt.md`; the design run writes `SPEC.md` into that folder.\n2. Hand-edit `SPEC.md`; add any `design-notes/`.\n3. Implement using the spec (save the implementation prompt as `02-implement.prompt.md`).\n4. Invoke `/archive-session` → renders + scrubs `transcript.md`, writes `statistics.md`,\n   scaffolds `analytics.md` (all from the session JSONL + captured rtk/ctx data).\n5. Optionally fill in `analytics.md`.\n6. Ask Claude to commit everything (code + session folder) in one commit; Claude writes\n   the message.\n\n## Reuse / alignment notes\n\n- Mirrors `prompts/` (reusable inputs) vs. new `sessions/` (per-run record); ignores\n  bulky/sensitive data by location like the rest of the repo.\n- Supersedes the single root `./SPEC.md` — a decision record per feature is exactly what\n  `sessions/<feature>/SPEC.md` now provides, accumulating.\n- Skill lives under the existing `.claude/` tooling dir, consistent with the repo's\n  AI-config placement.\n\n## Verification\n\n1. **Structure & sort:** `sessions/` with two dated folders sorts chronologically.\n2. **Render + scrub:** run `finalize-session.py` against a real session JSONL;\n   `transcript.md` is readable and\n   `grep -E 'SMTP_PASSWORD|AKIA|BEGIN [A-Z ]*PRIVATE KEY|Bearer ' sessions/**/transcript.md`\n   is empty, while the `transcript.raw.md` intermediate still contains the secrets.\n3. **Stats:** `statistics.md` shows correct per-model usage (spot-check vs JSONL),\n   session metadata, a cost estimate, an approximation-labeled context section, and the\n   rtk/ctx sections when those tools are present — cleanly omitted when absent.\n4. **Skill:** invoke `/archive-session` in a live session; confirm it captures `rtk gain`\n   and `ctx_stats`, runs the script, writes `transcript.md`/`statistics.md`, scaffolds\n   `analytics.md`, and does not commit.\n5. **Gitignore net:** `git check-ignore sessions/x/transcript.raw.txt` and\n   `sessions/x/session.jsonl` report ignored; `git status` shows `transcript.md`,\n   `statistics.md`, `SPEC.md`, prompts, `analytics.md` as trackable.\n6. **Template dry-run:** `new-feature-design.prompt-template.md` now writes into\n   `sessions/<date-slug>/SPEC.md` and creates the folder first.\n7. **End-to-end:** next real feature runs the full workflow and commits code + session\n   folder atomically.\n```\n",
  "planFilePath": "/home/node/.claude/plans/make-a-recommendation-here-keen-gadget.md"

## Assistant

Two good corrections. On the directory name: I'd actually push back gently on `development/` too — this repo (and the README TODO) leans hard on Pantheon's **Dev / Test / Live environment** terminology, so `development/` risks the same overloading problem as `sessions/`. Let me offer a couple of alternatives that dodge *both* collisions:

This\nplan adds the accumulating archive, the tooling to populate it, and a manually-invoked\nskill to orchestrate the end-of-session capture.\n\nTwo risks shaped it: (1) the tool is meant to be reusable by other institutions, so\nU-M dev history is noise to downstream cloners; (2) live secrets (`SMTP_PASSWORD`,\nPantheon machine token, `AWS_*`, `CLOUDFLARE_*`) flow through the environment and\ncommand output, so raw transcripts/logs can leak credentials — and `.gitignore`\ncatches none of that today.\n\n## Decisions (from the interview)\n\n- **Location:** committed top-level `development/` directory in **this** repo.\n- **Grouping:** one folder per feature/task cycle, `YYYY-MM-DD-slug`, chronologically\n  sortable. Multiple prompts/sessions for one feature nest inside it.\n- **Spec:** the spec is written **into the feature folder** — the same directory that\n  the initial design prompt lives in (`development/<date-slug>/SPEC.md`). *Mark will\n  update `new-feature-design.prompt-template.md` himself to say the spec is written to\n  the same directory as the initial prompt — that template edit is out of scope for\n  this plan.*\n- **Transcript source:** the skill renders the committed `transcript.md` **directly\n  from the session JSONL** (`~/.claude/projects/-workspace/*.jsonl`) — no manual\n  `/export` step; one skill invocation does everything. The JSONL itself is mined for\n  statistics but is **not committed** (gitignored). Trade-off accepted: this is our own\n  JSONL→markdown rendering, not Claude Code's official `/export` format, in exchange for\n  full one-command automation.\n- **Secret handling:** deterministic regex scrubbing in a Python script (not LLM\n  judgment), plus a `.gitignore` safety net so raw exports and JSONL logs can never be\n  committed by accident.\n- **Statistics:** auto-generated into `statistics.md` from the JSONL + in-session data:\n  session metadata, usage, cost estimate, context-window (approx), rtk gain, ctx-stats.\n- **Orchestration:** a manually-invoked Claude skill (`/archive-session`) that, at\n  session end, gathers in-session-only data, runs the script, and writes the artifacts\n  into the feature folder. Mark then asks Claude to commit everything (Claude writes the\n  commit message).\n- **Commit coupling:** the feature folder lands in the **same commit** as the code.\n\n## Target structure\n\n```\n.claude/skills/archive-session/SKILL.md   # manually-invoked orchestrator skill\ndevelopment/\n  README.md                               # the convention itself\n  finalize-session.py                     # deterministic render+scrub + stats assembly\n  2026-07-03-daily-traffic-alerts/\n    01-design.prompt.md                   # input: design prompt used\n    design-notes/                         # input: optional hand-authored design docs\n    SPEC.md                               # generated spec/plan, then hand-edited\n    02-implement.prompt.md                # input: implementation prompt used\n    transcript.md                         # rendered + scrubbed transcript (committed)\n    statistics.md                         # auto-generated session stats (committed)\n    analytics.md                          # optional hand-written analysis (scaffolded)\n  2026-07-20-sitelens-security-score/\n    ...\n```\n\nInside a feature folder: numeric prefixes (`01-`, `02-`) order prompt files; fixed\nnames for `SPEC.md`/`transcript.md`/`statistics.md`/`analytics.md`; multi-session work\nuses `transcript-01.md`/`statistics-01.md`, etc. `statistics.md` is machine-generated\n(don't hand-edit); `analytics.md` is Mark's narrative (skill scaffolds an empty\ntemplate). Slug prefers matching README TODO wording when applicable.\n\n## Component 1 — `development/finalize-session.py` (deterministic core)\n\nPlain-Python house style, no new deps, runnable standalone (testable outside a\nsession). Two jobs:\n\n**A. Render + scrub the transcript.** Read the session JSONL and render it to readable\nmarkdown (user/assistant turns, tool calls, tool results, thinking blocks), writing the\nunscrubbed intermediate as `transcript.raw.md` (gitignored). Then produce\n`transcript.md` with secrets redacted via regex — values of `SMTP_PASSWORD`,\n`AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID`/`AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY` (incl. `AKIA…` / 40-char secret shapes),\n`CLOUDFLARE_API_KEY`/`CLOUDFLARE_EMAIL`, Pantheon `machine_token`/`session`,\n`Bearer <token>` / `Authorization` headers, `-----BEGIN … PRIVATE KEY-----` blocks.\nBest-effort; README documents a manual grep backstop before commit. (May optionally\naccept a pre-run `/export` text as an override input for higher-fidelity formatting.)\n\n**B. Assemble `statistics.md`** from the session JSONL plus skill-supplied capture\nfiles. Sections, each nicely formatted:\n- **Session metadata:** date/time, duration, model(s), turn count, tool-call counts by\n  tool. *(From JSONL — reliable.)*\n- **Usage** (like `/usage`): per-model input / output / cache-read / cache-write token\n  totals, from each assistant turn's `usage` block. *(From JSONL — reliable, primary.)*\n- **Cost estimate:** prefer any per-message cost field in the JSONL; else tokens × a\n  maintained per-model price table. **Pricing source/table to be chosen and kept\n  current during implementation** — flag it.\n- **Context window** (like `/context`): best-effort reconstruction of final context by\n  role/tool, **labeled as an approximation** (exact live `/context` can't be\n  reproduced post-hoc).\n- **rtk gain:** embed the skill-captured `rtk gain` output if present (note: cumulative,\n  not strictly per-session). Omit cleanly if absent.\n- **context-mode** (like `/ctx-stats`): embed the skill-captured `ctx_stats` output if\n  present. Omit cleanly if absent.\n\nDegrades gracefully: any missing input → section omitted, never a crash.\n\n## Component 2 — `.claude/skills/archive-session/SKILL.md` (orchestrator)\n\nA project skill Mark invokes manually at session end (`/archive-session`). Because it\nruns *in* the live session it can reach tools the script can't. Steps:\n1. Determine/confirm the target `development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/` folder (argument, or\n   infer from the active SPEC/branch, or prompt).\n2. ## Approved Plan (edited by user):
# Convention + tooling for Claude session artifacts (`development/` + `/archive-session` skill)

## Context

Mark builds features with Claude in a repeatable cycle: write a prompt (+ optional
design docs) → Claude produces a spec/implementation plan → Mark reads and hand-edits
it → Mark prompts Claude to implement using the spec → at session end, capture a
transcript plus statistics/analytics. He wants all of it committed **as a historical
record** of what was asked, discussed, and decided — explicitly **not** a primary
source of documentation.

Today there's no home for this. Adjacent pieces exist: `prompts/` holds reusable
prompt *templates*; `new-feature-design.prompt-template.md` writes a spec — but to a
single fixed `./SPEC.md` at repo root that every feature overwrites, so nothing
accumulates. `docs/` is end-user docs only; CLAUDE.md is non-obvious internals. This
plan adds the accumulating archive, the tooling to populate it, and a manually-invoked
skill to orchestrate the end-of-session capture.

Two risks shaped it: (1) the tool is meant to be reusable by other institutions, so
U-M dev history is noise to downstream cloners; (2) live secrets (`SMTP_PASSWORD`,
Pantheon machine token, `AWS_*`, `CLOUDFLARE_*`) flow through the environment and
command output, so raw transcripts/logs can leak credentials — and `.gitignore`
catches none of that today.

## Decisions (from the interview)

- **Location:** committed top-level `development/` directory in **this** repo.
- **Grouping:** one folder per feature/task cycle, `YYYY-MM-DD-slug`, chronologically
  sortable. Multiple prompts/sessions for one feature nest inside it.
- **Spec:** the spec is written **into the feature folder** — the same directory that
  the initial design prompt lives in (`development/<date-slug>/SPEC.md`). *Mark will
  update `new-feature-design.prompt-template.md` himself to say the spec is written to
  the same directory as the initial prompt — that template edit is out of scope for
  this plan.*
- **Transcript source:** the skill renders the committed `transcript.md` **directly
  from the session JSONL** (`~/.claude/projects/-workspace/*.jsonl`) — no manual
  `/export` step; one skill invocation does everything. The JSONL itself is mined for
  statistics but is **not committed** (gitignored). Trade-off accepted: this is our own
  JSONL→markdown rendering, not Claude Code's official `/export` format, in exchange for
  full one-command automation.
- **Secret handling:** deterministic regex scrubbing in a Python script (not LLM
  judgment), plus a `.gitignore` safety net so raw exports and JSONL logs can never be
  committed by accident.
- **Statistics:** auto-generated into `statistics.md` from the JSONL + in-session data:
  session metadata, usage, cost estimate, context-window (approx), rtk gain, ctx-stats.
- **Orchestration:** a manually-invoked Claude skill (`/archive-session`) that, at
  session end, gathers in-session-only data, runs the script, and writes the artifacts
  into the feature folder. Mark then asks Claude to commit everything (Claude writes the
  commit message).
- **Commit coupling:** the feature folder lands in the **same commit** as the code.

## Target structure

```
.claude/skills/archive-session/SKILL.md   # manually-invoked orchestrator skill
development/
  README.md                               # the convention itself
  finalize-session.py                     # deterministic render+scrub + stats assembly
  2026-07-03-daily-traffic-alerts/
    01-design.prompt.md                   # input: design prompt used
    design-notes/                         # input: optional hand-authored design docs
    SPEC.md                               # generated spec/plan, then hand-edited
    02-implement.prompt.md                # input: implementation prompt used
    transcript.md                         # rendered + scrubbed transcript (committed)
    statistics.md                         # auto-generated session stats (committed)
    analytics.md                          # optional hand-written analysis (scaffolded)
  2026-07-20-sitelens-security-score/
    ...
```

Inside a feature folder: numeric prefixes (`01-`, `02-`) order prompt files; fixed
names for `SPEC.md`/`transcript.md`/`statistics.md`/`analytics.md`; multi-session work
uses `transcript-01.md`/`statistics-01.md`, etc. `statistics.md` is machine-generated
(don't hand-edit); `analytics.md` is Mark's narrative (skill scaffolds an empty
template). Slug prefers matching README TODO wording when applicable.

## Component 1 — `development/finalize-session.py` (deterministic core)

Plain-Python house style, no new deps, runnable standalone (testable outside a
session). Two jobs:

**A. Render + scrub the transcript.** Read the session JSONL and render it to readable
markdown (user/assistant turns, tool calls, tool results, thinking blocks), writing the
unscrubbed intermediate as `transcript.raw.md` (gitignored). Then produce
`transcript.md` with secrets redacted via regex — values of `SMTP_PASSWORD`,
`AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID`/`AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY` (incl. `AKIA…` / 40-char secret shapes),
`CLOUDFLARE_API_KEY`/`CLOUDFLARE_EMAIL`, Pantheon `machine_token`/`session`,
`Bearer <token>` / `Authorization` headers, `-----BEGIN … PRIVATE KEY-----` blocks.
Best-effort; README documents a manual grep backstop before commit. (May optionally
accept a pre-run `/export` text as an override input for higher-fidelity formatting.)

**B. Assemble `statistics.md`** from the session JSONL plus skill-supplied capture
files. Sections, each nicely formatted:
- **Session metadata:** date/time, duration, model(s), turn count, tool-call counts by
  tool. *(From JSONL — reliable.)*
- **Usage** (like `/usage`): per-model input / output / cache-read / cache-write token
  totals, from each assistant turn's `usage` block. *(From JSONL — reliable, primary.)*
- **Cost estimate:** prefer any per-message cost field in the JSONL; else tokens × a
  maintained per-model price table. **Pricing source/table to be chosen and kept
  current during implementation** — flag it.
- **Context window** (like `/context`): best-effort reconstruction of final context by
  role/tool, **labeled as an approximation** (exact live `/context` can't be
  reproduced post-hoc).
- **rtk gain:** embed the skill-captured `rtk gain` output if present (note: cumulative,
  not strictly per-session). Omit cleanly if absent.
- **context-mode** (like `/ctx-stats`): embed the skill-captured `ctx_stats` output if
  present. Omit cleanly if absent.

Degrades gracefully: any missing input → section omitted, never a crash.

## Component 2 — `.claude/skills/archive-session/SKILL.md` (orchestrator)

A project skill Mark invokes manually at session end (`/archive-session`). Because it
runs *in* the live session it can reach tools the script can't. Steps:
1. Determine/confirm the target `development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/` folder (argument, or
   infer from the active SPEC/branch, or prompt).
2. Capture in-session-only data to gitignored `*.raw.txt` files: run `rtk gain` via Bash
   (if `rtk` on PATH); call the context-mode `ctx_stats` MCP tool (if configured).
3. Run `finalize-session.py`, passing the folder + capture files → it renders + scrubs
   `transcript.md` from the newest session JSONL and assembles `statistics.md`.
4. Scaffold an empty `analytics.md` template for Mark's narrative (if absent).
5. Report what was written; do **not** commit. Mark then asks Claude to commit
   everything (Claude writes the commit message).

Rationale for the script/skill split: scrubbing and number-crunching stay deterministic
and testable in Python (never trust an LLM to reliably redact a credential or format
token math); the skill only does what genuinely needs the live session (capturing
`ctx_stats`/`rtk gain`, wiring paths, scaffolding). No git pre-commit hook — the skill
is per-session, invoked on demand.

## Other files to create / modify

- **`development/README.md` (new)** — authoritative convention: folder naming, canonical
  files/roles, end-to-end workflow (below), "record, not documentation" caveat,
  same-commit rule, how `/archive-session` and `finalize-session.py` fit together, and
  the manual secret-review grep.
- **`.gitignore` (modify)** — add near the working-data patterns:
  ```
  # Claude development archive: keep scrubbed artifacts, never raw exports or logs
  /development/**/*.raw.txt
  /development/**/*.raw.md
  /development/**/*.jsonl
  ```
- **`CLAUDE.md` (modify, root)** — short "Development archive" subsection pointing to
  `development/README.md`: what the archive is, the `YYYY-MM-DD-slug` rule, that it's a
  record and **not** documentation, that transcripts are scrubbed via `/archive-session`
  before commit, that the JSONL is never committed, and that the folder commits
  atomically with the code.
- *(Out of scope — Mark handles):* `prompts/new-feature-design.prompt-template.md` edit
  to write `SPEC.md` into the same directory as the initial prompt.

## End-to-end workflow (documented in `development/README.md`)

1. Start a feature: create `development/<date-slug>/`, drop the design prompt in as
   `01-design.prompt.md`; the design run writes `SPEC.md` into that folder.
2. Hand-edit `SPEC.md`; add any `design-notes/`.
3. Implement using the spec (save the implementation prompt as `02-implement.prompt.md`).
4. Invoke `/archive-session` → renders + scrubs `transcript.md`, writes `statistics.md`,
   scaffolds `analytics.md` (all from the session JSONL + captured rtk/ctx data).
5. Optionally fill in `analytics.md`.
6. Ask Claude to commit everything (code + feature folder) in one commit; Claude writes
   the message.

## Reuse / alignment notes

- Mirrors `prompts/` (reusable inputs) vs. new `development/` (per-run record); ignores
  bulky/sensitive data by location like the rest of the repo.
- Supersedes the single root `./SPEC.md` — a decision record per feature is exactly what
  `development/<feature>/SPEC.md` now provides, accumulating.
- Skill lives under the existing `.claude/` tooling dir, consistent with the repo's
  AI-config placement.

## Verification

1. **Structure & sort:** `development/` with two dated folders sorts chronologically.
2. **Render + scrub:** run `finalize-session.py` against a real session JSONL;
   `transcript.md` is readable and
   `grep -E 'SMTP_PASSWORD|AKIA|BEGIN [A-Z ]*PRIVATE KEY|Bearer ' development/**/transcript.md`
   is empty, while the `transcript.raw.md` intermediate still contains the secrets.
3. **Stats:** `statistics.md` shows correct per-model usage (spot-check vs JSONL),
   session metadata, a cost estimate, an approximation-labeled context section, and the
   rtk/ctx sections when those tools are present — cleanly omitted when absent.
4. **Skill:** invoke `/archive-session` in a live session; confirm it captures `rtk gain`
   and `ctx_stats`, runs the script, writes `transcript.md`/`statistics.md`, scaffolds
   `analytics.md`, and does not commit.
5. **Gitignore net:** `git check-ignore development/x/transcript.raw.md` and
   `development/x/session.jsonl` report ignored; `git status` shows `transcript.md`,
   `statistics.md`, `SPEC.md`, prompts, `analytics.md` as trackable.
6. **End-to-end:** next real feature runs the full workflow and commits code + feature
   folder atomically.

### ↳ Tool result

```
```python

import os, json, glob
from collections import Counter, defaultdict

d = os.path.expanduser("~/.claude/projects/-workspace")
files = sorted(glob.glob(os.path.join(d, "*.jsonl")), key=os.path.getmtime)
print("num jsonl files:", len(files))
for f in files[-5:]:
    print(f"{os.path.getsize(f):>10}  {os.path.basename(f)}")

newest = files[-1]
print("\nNEWEST:", os.path.basename(newest))
lines = open(newest, encoding="utf-8").read().splitlines()
print("num lines:", len(lines))

# top-level key sets and 'type' values
type_counter = Counter()
toplevel_keys = Counter()
sample_by_type = {}
for ln in lines:
    if not ln.strip(): continue
    try: obj = json.loads(ln)
    except: continue
    t = obj.get("type")
    type_counter[t]+=1
    toplevel_keys[tuple(sorted(obj.keys()))]+=1
    if t not in sample_by_type:
        sample_by_type[t]=obj

print("\ntype counts:", dict(type_counter))
print("\ntop-level key combos:")
for k,c in toplevel_keys.most_common():
    print(" ", c, k)

```

```python

import os, json, glob
from collections import Counter

d = os.path.expanduser("~/.claude/projects/-workspace")
files = sorted(glob.glob(os.path.join(d, "*.jsonl")), key=os.path.getmtime)
newest = files[-1]
lines = [json.loads(l) for l in open(newest, encoding="utf-8") if l.strip()]

# message.content block types by role
block_types = Counter()
usage_keys = Counter()
models = Counter()
cost_fields_present = Counter()
ts_first=ts_last=None

def blocks(msg):
    c = msg.get("content")
    if isinstance(c, str): return [{"type":"__string__"}]
    if isinstance(c, list): return c
    return []

for o in lines:
    t=o.get("type")
    if t in ("user","assistant") and isinstance(o.get("message"),dict):
        m=o["message"]
        for b in blocks(m):
            block_types[(t, b.get("type"))]+=1
        if t=="assistant":
            u=m.get("usage") or {}
            for k in u: usage_keys[k]+=1
            if m.get("model"): models[m["model"]]+=1
        # any cost field?
        for k in ("costUSD","cost","totalCostUsd"):
            if k in o or k in m: cost_fields_present[k]+=1
    ts=o.get("timestamp")
    if ts:
        ts_first = ts_first or ts
        ts_last = ts

print("block types (role,type):")
for k,c in block_types.most_common(): print("  ",c,k)
print("\nusage keys:", dict(usage_keys))
print("models:", dict(models))
print("cost fields present:", dict(cost_fields_present))
print("ts_first:", ts_first, " ts_last:", ts_last)

# show one assistant usage block, one tool_use block, one tool_result shape
for o in lines:
    m=o.get("message") if isinstance(o.get("message"),dict) else {}
    if o.get("type")=="assistant" and m.get("usage"):
        print("\nSAMPLE usage:", json.dumps(m["usage"]))
        break
for o in lines:

    for b in (m.get("content") or []) if isinstance(m.get("content"),list) else []:
        if isinstance(b,dict) and b.get("type")=="tool_use":
            print("SAMPLE t

## Assistant

Schema is clear now. Key facts for the implementation:
- `user`/`assistant` lines carry a `message` (role, `content` as string or blocks: `text`/`thinking`/`tool_use`/`tool_result`), assistant lines carry `usage` + `model` (`claude-opus-4-8`).
- **No cost field in the JSONL** → I must compute cost from tokens × a price table. So I need accurate current pricing. Let me consult the claude-api skill for that (it's the authoritative source, and the harness rules require it for pricing).
- Timestamps are ISO8601 → duration from first/last. `isSidechain` marks subagent turns.

Let me pull pricing and set up task tracking in parallel.

## User

Base directory for this skill: /tmp/claude-501/bundled-skills/2.1.199/5f9524677d52584ecfc34d3ef70ea826/claude-api

# Building LLM-Powered Applications with Claude

This skill helps you build LLM-powered applications with Claude. Choose the right surface based on your needs, detect the project language, then read the relevant language-specific documentation.

## Before You Start

Scan the target file (or, if no target file, the prompt and project) for non-Anthropic provider markers — `import openai`, `from openai`, `langchain_openai`, `OpenAI(`, `gpt-4`, `gpt-5`, file names like `agent-openai.py` or `*-generic.py`, or any explicit instruction to keep the code provider-neutral. If you find any, stop and tell the user that this skill produces Claude/Anthropic SDK code; ask whether they want to switch the file to Claude or want a non-Claude implementation. Do not edit a non-Anthropic file with Anthropic SDK calls.

## Output Requirement

When the user asks you to add, modify, or implement a Claude feature, your code must call Claude through one of:

1. **The official Anthropic SDK** for the project's language (`anthropic`, `@anthropic-ai/sdk`, `com.anthropic.*`, etc.). This is the default whenever a supported SDK exists for the project.
2. **Raw HTTP** (`curl`, `requests`, `fetch`, `httpx`, etc.) — only when the user explicitly asks for cURL/REST/raw HTTP, the project is a shell/cURL project, or the language has no official SDK.

Never mix the two — don't reach for `requests`/`fetch` in a Python or TypeScript project just because it feels lighter. Never fall back to OpenAI-compatible shims.

**Never guess SDK usage.** Function names, class names, namespaces, method signatures, and import paths must come from explicit documentation — either the `{lang}/` files in this skill or the official SDK repositories or documentation links listed in `shared/live-sources.md`. If the binding you need is not explicitly documented in the skill files, WebFetch the relevant SDK repo from `shared/live-sources.md` before writing code. Do not infer Ruby/Java/Go/PHP/C# APIs from cURL shapes or from another language's SDK.

**If WebFetch or repository access fails** (network restricted, timeouts, clone blocked): do not keep retrying — write code from the patterns and namespace/package tables in the `{lang}/` file, run the compiler or interpreter on it, and iterate on the error output. For statically-typed SDKs (C#, Java, Go) a compile-fix loop against local errors reaches working code faster than blocked network research.

## Defaults

Unless the user requests otherwise:

For the Claude model version, please use Claude Opus 4.8, which you can access via the exact model string `claude-opus-4-8`. Please default to using adaptive thinking (`thinking: {type: "adaptive"}`) for anything remotely complicated. And finally, please default to streaming for any request that may involve long input, long output, or high `max_tokens` — it prevents hitting request timeouts. Use the SDK's `.get_final_message()` / `.finalMessage()` helper to get the complete response if you don't need to handle individual stream events

## ⚠️ API Drift — Your Training Prior May Be Stale

Several common Claude API shapes changed in 2025–2026. If you recall a pattern from training, verify it against the `{lang}/` files in this skill before writing — the rows below are the most frequent drift points:

| Area | Stale prior | Current API |
|---|---|---|
| Extended thinking | `thinking: {type: "enabled", budget_tokens: N}` | On Claude 4.6+ models: `thinking: {type: "adaptive"}`. `budget_tokens` is deprecated on Opus 4.6 / Sonnet 4.6 and **rejected with a 400** on Fable 5 / Sonnet 5 / Opus 4.8 / 4.7. Pre-4.6 models still use `budget_tokens`. |
| Web search / web fetch tool type | `web_search_20250305`, `web_fetch_20250910` | `web_search_20260209`, `web_fetch_20260209` (dynamic filtering) on Opus 4.8/4.7/4.6, Sonnet 5, and Sonnet 4.6. Older models keep the basic variants; on Vertex AI only basic `web_search_20250305` is available (web fetch is not on Vertex) — see the Server Tools QR below. |
| PHP parameter names | snake_case wire names as named args (`max_tokens`) | Top-level named args are camelCase (`maxTokens`). Nested array keys vary by feature (e.g. `'taskBudget'`, `'skillID'`, `'mcp_server_name'`) — copy the exact key from the documented example; do not bulk-convert. |

The `{lang}/` files in this skill are authoritative over recalled patterns.
