### ⚙ Tool call: `Write`

```json
{
  "file_path": "/workspace/development/README.md",
  "content": "# `development/` — Claude session archive\n\nThis directory is a committed, **historical record** of how features were built with\nClaude: the prompts used, the specs produced and hand-edited, scrubbed session\ntranscripts, and per-session statistics. It is a record of what was asked, discussed,\nand decided — **not a primary source of documentation.** For how the code actually\nworks, read the code, the root `CLAUDE.md`, and `docs/`.\n\n## Layout — one folder per feature\n\n```\ndevelopment/\n  README.md                 # this file\n  finalize-session.py       # renders+scrubs transcripts and builds statistics\n  2026-07-03-daily-traffic-alerts/\n    01-design.prompt.md      # input: the design prompt used\n    design-notes/            # input: optional hand-authored design docs\n    SPEC.md                  # generated spec/plan, then hand-edited\n    02-implement.prompt.md   # input: the implementation prompt used\n    transcript.md            # rendered + secret-scrubbed transcript (committed)\n    statistics.md            # auto-generated session stats (committed; don't hand-edit)\n    analytics.md             # your narrative analysis (optional, hand-written)\n```\n\nConventions:\n- **Folder name:** `YYYY-MM-DD-slug`, so folders sort chronologically. Prefer a slug\n  that matches the relevant `README.md` TODO wording when the work maps to one.\n- **Prompt ordering:** number prompt files `01-`, `02-`, … in the order they were used.\n- **Fixed names:** `SPEC.md`, `transcript.md`, `statistics.md`, `analytics.md`.\n- **Multiple sessions for one feature:** suffix the per-session files —\n  `transcript-01.md` / `statistics-01.md`, `transcript-02.md`, … A single-session\n  feature leaves them unsuffixed.\n- **`statistics.md` is machine-generated** — don't hand-edit it. Put your own\n  commentary in `analytics.md`.\n\n## Two safety rules\n\n1. **Transcripts are scrubbed of secrets before commit.** This repo's live secrets\n   (`SMTP_PASSWORD`, the Pantheon machine token, `AWS_*`, `CLOUDFLARE_*`) flow through\n   the environment and command output, so a raw transcript can leak credentials.\n   `finalize-session.py` redacts the known patterns; as a backstop, before committing,\n   eyeball:\n   ```\n   grep -rE 'SMTP_PASSWORD|AKIA|BEGIN [A-Z ]*PRIVATE KEY|Bearer ' development/<dir>/\n   ```\n2. **The raw session JSONL is never committed.** It's the data source for statistics,\n   but it's bulky and secret-heavy. `.gitignore` blocks `development/**/*.jsonl`,\n   `*.raw.md`, and `*.raw.txt` so raw exports/logs can't be committed by accident.\n\n## End-to-end workflow\n\n1. Create `development/<date-slug>/`; save the design prompt as `01-design.prompt.md`.\n   The design run writes `SPEC.md` into that folder. (Per the project's\n   `new-feature-design.prompt-template.md`, the spec is written to the same directory\n   as the initial prompt.)\n2. Hand-edit `SPEC.md`; add any `design-notes/`.\n3. Implement using the spec; save the implementation prompt as `02-implement.prompt.md`.\n4. Run **`/archive-session`** (the skill). It renders + scrubs `transcript.md`, writes\n   `statistics.md`, and scaffolds `analytics.md` — from the session JSONL plus captured\n   `rtk gain` / `/ctx-stats` output.\n5. Optionally fill in `analytics.md`.\n6. Ask Claude to commit everything — the code **and** `development/<date-slug>/` — in a\n   single commit (Claude writes the message).\n\n## `finalize-session.py`\n\nThe deterministic core the skill drives (also runnable by hand). It:\n- renders the newest Claude Code session JSONL to readable markdown, writes the\n  unscrubbed `transcript.raw.md` (gitignored), then the scrubbed `transcript.md`;\n- assembles `statistics.md`: session metadata (duration, models, turns, tool-call\n  counts), usage (per-model token totals), an estimated cost (token counts × a price\n  table maintained in the script — the JSONL records no cost), an approximate context\n  size, and the captured `rtk gain` / `/ctx-stats` sections when present.\n\n```\npython development/finalize-session.py --dir development/<date-slug> \\\n    [--jsonl <path>] [--rtk-capture <file>] [--ctx-capture <file>] \\\n    [--transcript-input <export.txt>] [--label NN]\n```\n\n`--transcript-input` scrubs a pre-run `/export` text instead of rendering the JSONL,\nif you want Claude Code's official transcript formatting. Keep the price table in the\nscript current when model prices change — `statistics.md` prints the pricing date it used.\n"
}
```

All verified. Here's what I built for the `development/` archive convention, matching the approved plan.

## What's in place

**`development/finalize-session.py`** — the deterministic core (stdlib-only, standalone, executable):
- Renders the newest session JSONL → readable `transcript.raw.md` (gitignored) → secret-scrubbed `transcript.md`. Scrub self-test redacts `SMTP_PASSWORD`, `AKIA…`, Bearer tokens, Pantheon `machine_token`, PEM keys, and Cloudflare keys with **zero leaks**.
- Assembles `statistics.md`: metadata (duration, models, turns, tool-call counts), per-model usage, an **estimated cost** (token counts × a maintained price table, since the JSONL has no cost field — Opus 4.8 at $5/$25 with 5m/1h cache-write and cache-read multipliers, splitting 5m vs 1h from the usage block), an approximation-labeled context size, and `rtk gain` / `/ctx-stats` sections that omit cleanly when absent. On this very session it computed 70 turns and ~$17.83.

**`.claude/skills/archive-session/SKILL.md`** — the manually-invoked `/archive-session` orchestrator: locates the feature folder, captures `rtk gain` (Bash) and `ctx_stats` (MCP tool) to gitignored `*.raw.txt`, runs the script, scaffolds `analytics.md`, verifies the scrub grep, and reports **without committing**.

**`development/README.md`** — the authoritative convention (layout, naming, the two safety rules, end-to-end workflow).

**`.gitignore`** — safety net: `development/**/*.raw.txt`, `*.raw.md`, `*.jsonl` ignored; `transcript.md`/`statistics.md`/`SPEC.md`/`analytics.md` tracked. Verified with `git check-ignore` both directions.

**`CLAUDE.md`** — a short "Development archive" subsection pointing future sessions at the convention.

## Notes
- The `new-feature-design.prompt-template.md` edit is **yours** to make (spec → same dir as the initial prompt), per your decision — I left it untouched.
- Two things worth knowing when you exercise it for real: `statistics.md` prints the pricing date it used, so keep the `PRICES` table in the script current; and the context-window section is explicitly labeled an approximation (it's reconstructed from the JSONL post-hoc).

Nothing is committed — the working tree shows the 5 changes staged for whenever you want them. I didn't run `/archive-session` against this planning session itself, but the script it calls is verified end-to-end.

## User

Can the skill invoke the `/usage` command in order to get pricing information and other statistics from it to include in the archive files?  This would avoid the need for a pricing table and the need to keep that table up to date.

## Assistant

Short answer up front: **no — the skill can't invoke `/usage` (or `/cost`, `/context`, `/export`) and capture its output.** Those are built-in Claude Code CLI commands handled by the harness, not tools or skills the model can call. The Skill tool is explicit about this ("Do not use this tool for built-in CLI commands like /help, /clear"). It's the same reason we render the transcript from the JSONL instead of driving `/export`.

But your underlying goal — kill the price table so there's nothing to keep current — is worth solving properly. Let me confirm the exact Claude Code behavior (what `/usage` vs `/cost` actually show, and whether any programmatic path exists) before I recommend, rather than guess.

### ⚙ Tool call: `Agent`

```json
{
  "subagent_type": "claude-code-guide",
  "description": "Confirm slash-command access + cost data",
  "run_in_background": false,
  "prompt": "I'm building a Claude Code skill (a user-invocable SKILL.md) that finalizes a coding session by writing archive files, including session statistics. I need precise, current facts — please verify against Claude Code docs/behavior, don't guess:\n\n1. Can a skill (invoked via the Skill tool by the model) programmatically invoke a BUILT-IN slash command such as `/usage`, `/cost`, `/context`, or `/export`, and capture that command's rendered output for use in the skill? My understanding is NO — these are harness-handled CLI commands, not tools/MCP endpoints the model can call, and the Skill tool explicitly excludes built-in CLI commands. Confirm or correct.\n\n2. What does each of these actually DISPLAY, specifically:\n   - `/usage` — is it subscription/plan rate-limit consumption, or per-session dollar cost, or both?\n   - `/cost` — does it show the current session's dollar cost and token breakdown? For which account types (API/console billing vs Max/Pro subscription)? Does `/cost` show a dollar figure for subscription users, or only for API-key/console users?\n   - `/context` — what breakdown does it show?\n\n3. Is there ANY programmatic or machine-readable way, from within a Claude Code session or from its on-disk data, to obtain the session's DOLLAR cost (not just token counts)? Specifically:\n   - Does the session transcript JSONL under ~/.claude/projects/ contain any per-message or per-session cost field (e.g. costUSD, totalCostUsd)? (In the file I inspected, assistant messages had a `usage` block with token counts but I saw no cost field.)\n   - Is there an environment variable, hook payload field, statusline input field, or MCP tool that exposes session cost in dollars?\n   - Does the Claude Models API (GET /v1/models/{id}) return per-token pricing? (I believe it returns context window and capabilities but not price.)\n\n4. Is there a documented/official way for a skill or script to get current per-token model PRICING without hardcoding a table (any API endpoint, bundled data file, or CLI command)?\n\nGive me concrete, sourced answers. Where something is version-dependent or uncertain, say so. Keep it focused on these questions."
}
```

### ↳ Tool result

```
Based on my research of official Claude Code and Claude API documentation, here are your answers:

## 1. Can a skill programmatically invoke built-in slash commands?

**NO.** Skills cannot invoke built-in slash commands like `/usage`, `/cost`, `/context`, or `/export`.

Per the [Claude Code Skills documentation](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/skills.md):
- Skills are prompt-based workflows that load instructions into context; they run through the existing `Skill` tool
- Built-in commands are "hardcoded into the Claude Code CLI" as fixed-logic operations handled by the harness
- The docs explicitly separate these: "For built-in commands like `/help` and `/compact`, and bundled skills like `/debug` and `/code-review`, see the [commands reference](/en/commands)."
- Skills extend Claude's capabilities through prompts; they do not have access to invoke CLI slash commands

## 2. What does each command actually display?

**`/usage` (alias: `/cost`)**
Per [Manage costs effectively](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/costs.md):
- Shows detailed token usage statistics for the current session (input, output, cached tokens)
- For **API users**: displays a dollar figure "estimated locally from token counts" and may differ from your actual bill
- For **Pro/Max/Team/Enterprise subscribers**: shows plan usage limits/bars, activity stats, and a breakdown attributing usage to skills, subagents, plugins, and MCP servers (approximate, computed from local session history on this machine only)
- Does NOT show subscription rate limits or plan consumption — only session-level metrics and subscriber usage attribution

**`/context`**
Per [Explore the context window](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/context-window.md): shows what is consuming space in your context window with a breakdown of system prompt (~4200 tokens), auto memory, environment info, MCP tool schemas, CLAUDE.md, skills, JSONL transcript, etc., displayed as an interactive visualization.

**`/export`**
Per [Manage sessions](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/sessions.md): opens a menu to copy the current conversation to clipboard or save as a plain-text file with messages and tool outputs rendered as readable text. The underlying JSONL format is internal and changes between versions; `/export` is the recommended interface.

## 3. Programmatic access to session dollar cost

**No documented way exists within Claude Code sessions.** Specifics:

- **Session JSONL transcript**: Contains `message.usage` with token counts (input_tokens, output_tokens, cache_creation_input_tokens, cache_read_input_tokens) but **NO cost field**. Per the docs: "The entry format is internal to Claude Code and changes between versions, so scripts that parse these files directly can break on any release."
- **Environment variables, hooks, MCP tools**: None expose per-session dollar cost
- **Claude Models API** (`GET /v1/models/{id}`): Returns capabilities and context windows—**not pricing data**
- **For organization/team API cost tracking**: The [Usage & Cost Admin API](https://platform.claude.com/docs/en/manage-claude/usage-cost-api.md) provides historical cost data in USD, but requires an Admin API key and is organization-level only (unavailable for individual accounts)
- **For Claude Code per-user costs**: Reference the [Claude Code Analytics API](https://platform.claude.com/docs/en/manage-claude/claude-code-analytics-api.md) (mentioned in the Usage & Cost API docs), which provides per-user estimated costs without Admin API overhead

## 4. Programmatic access to current per-token pricing

**NO documented/official API exists.** Details:

- The Claude Models API does not return pricing
- The Usage & Cost Admin API returns *historical* costs (USD totals), not current price tables
- The [Pricing page](https://claude.com/pricing) is the public source for model pricing
- **Anthropic does not provide a programmatic pricing API or price-fetch endpoint**

For a skill, you must either:
1. Hardcode a pricing table in your skill's instructions/logic
2. Fetch https://claude.com/pricing via WebFetch and parse it (fragile; HTML changes break it)
3. Rely on the Usage & Cost Admin API if you have org-level access

---

**Summary for your skill**: You cannot capture `/usage` output programmatically from within a skill. Instead, use the session JSONL (read via a script/hook outside the skill) to extract token counts, then compute cost locally with a hardcoded pricing table. For per-user cost attribution, prefer the Claude Code Analytics API if available to your account tier.

Sources:
- [Claude Code Commands Reference](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/commands.md)
- [Manage costs effectively](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/costs.md)
- [Explore the context window](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/context-window.md)
- [Manage sessions](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/sessions.md)
- [Extend Claude with skills](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/skills.md)
- [Usage and Cost API](https://platform.claude.com/docs/en/manage-claude/usage-cost-api.md)
- [Claude Models API](https://platform.claude.com/docs/en/api/models.md)
agentId: a7d68db510f0e679a (use SendMessage with to: 'a7d68db510f0e679a', summary: '<5-10 word recap>' to continue this agent)
<usage>subagent_tokens: 50759
tool_uses: 17
duration_ms: 118380</usage>
```

## Assistant

Confirmed, and there's a nuance that actually settles the design question. Key findings from the Claude Code docs:

- **`/usage` and `/cost` are the same command**, and for API-billed usage it shows a dollar figure **"estimated locally from token counts."** So `/usage` isn't a more authoritative price source — Claude Code computes cost from its *own* bundled price table, exactly like our script does. Invoking it (even if we could) wouldn't eliminate a table; it'd just move the table into Claude Code's binary.
- **There's no programmatic price source at all**: the JSONL has no cost field, no env var / hook / MCP exposes session cost, and the Models API returns capabilities but not pricing. The only official USD source is the org-level **Usage & Cost Admin API** (needs an Admin API key — heavyweight, probably not worth it for this tool).

So the honest situation: *someone* maintains a price table — us, or Claude Code. There's no free lunch. Given that, here's how to best serve your actual goal (nothing to keep updated in this repo):

### ⚙ Tool call: `AskUserQuestion`

    {

      "header": "Cost source",
      "multiSelect": false,
      "options": [
        {

          "description": "Remove the price table + cost math from finalize-session.py. The skill asks you to run /usage and paste its output into usage.raw.txt (gitignored); the script embeds it verbatim, exactly like the rtk gain / ctx-stats captures. Dollar figure comes from Claude Code's own numbers; nothing to maintain here. Cost: one paste per archive.",
          "preview": "skill: 'run /usage, paste the output'\n  -> development/<dir>/usage.raw.txt (gitignored)\nstatistics.md embeds it verbatim under 'Usage & cost'\ntoken counts still auto-extracted from the JSONL\nNO price table in the repo"

## 1. Skill vs Custom Command: Which for this workflow?

**Either works identically; skill is the right vehicle for THIS workflow.**

Per [Extend Claude with skills](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/skills.md):
&gt; "Custom commands have been merged into skills. A file at `.claude/commands/deploy.md` and a skill at `.claude/skills/deploy/SKILL.md` both create `/deploy` and work the same way."

**Concrete differences for your workflow:**

| Feature | Skill (`.claude/skills/`) | Command (`.claude/commands/`) |
|---------|-------------------------|------------------------------|
| **Invocation** | `/archive-session` or `/archive-session arg1 arg2` | `/archive-session` or `/archive-session arg1 arg2` |
| **Helper files** | ✓ Directory `archive-session/` can hold scripts, data files | ✗ Flat file; must reference external paths |
| **Progressive loading** | ✓ `SKILL.md` loads only when invoked; context cost zero until used | ✓ Same |
| **Frontmatter control** | ✓ `disable-model-invocation`, `allowed-tools`, `argument-hint`, `$ARGUMENTS` substitution | ✓ Same (v2.1.196+) |
| **$ARGUMENTS, !bash, @file** | ✓ Full support | ✓ Same |

**For your end-of-session archive:** A skill is **not overkill**—it's ideal because:
- You get a directory to bundle the Python script alongside `SKILL.md`
- `disable-model-invocation: true` enforces manual typing (prevents Claude from auto-running)
- `$ARGUMENTS` lets you pass folder/slug as `/archive-session reports/2026-q3`
- `allowed-tools` can whitelist only the tools needed (Bash, Read, if needed)

The `.claude/skills/` placement already commits it to this repo only, which is correct for project-specific conventions.

## 2. Plugins: Alternative or distribution wrapper?

**Neither—plugins are a *distribution and organization wrapper* for skills, commands, agents, hooks, and MCP servers.** They are not an alternative.

Per [Create plugins](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/plugins.md):
&gt; "Plugins let you extend Claude Code with custom functionality that can be shared across projects and teams."

And the key distinction:

| Approach | Best for | Skill namespace |
|----------|----------|-----------------|
| **Standalone** (`.claude/` dir) | Personal workflows, project-specific customizations | `/archive-session` |
| **Plugins** (self-contained with `plugin.json` manifest) | Sharing with teammates, community distribution, reuse across projects | `/my-plugin:archive-session` |

**Your use case:** Stay standalone in `.claude/skills/` (project-specific script + convention). Convert to a plugin only if you want to:
- Share across all your personal projects (package as `~/.claude/skills/my-archive-plugin/` with `plugin.json`)
- Distribute via marketplace
- Version and release independently

## 3. Hooks: Why NOT for this workflow

**A hook is a poor fit; skill is correct.** Here's why:

Per [Hooks documentation](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/hooks.md):
&gt; **Hooks are NOT interactive.** They "run in the background with no controlling terminal (`/dev/tty` unavailable), no ability to open dialogs, no stdin from the user."

| Aspect | Hooks | Skills |
|--------|-------|--------|
| **Triggered** | Automatic at lifecycle points (SessionEnd, PreToolUse, etc) | User-initiated (`/archive-session`) or Claude-decided |
| **User input** | Cannot request—runs headless | Can ask Claude to prompt user for folder, yes/no confirmation |
| **Judgment calls** | No—runs conditionally but no reasoning | Full Claude reasoning for folder selection, cleanup decisions |
| **Interactive paste** | ✗ No way to ask user to paste `/usage` output | ✓ Can ask Claude to request it interactively |

**Why SessionEnd hook would be wrong:**
- Runs *automatically* at session end; you explicitly want manual control ("near the end, TYPE something")
- Cannot interactively ask the user to paste `/usage` output or confirm folder/slug—it's headless
- No way to ask "do you want to include draft sections?" or "override existing archive?"—just fixed logic

**Verdict:** Skill is the idiomatic choice for interactive, judgment-driven workflows. Hooks are for policy enforcement and background automation.

## 4. Project-level vs User-level placement

**Current placement (`.claude/skills/` in repo) is correct for project-specific logic.**

From [Create plugins](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/plugins.md):
&gt; Use standalone configuration when "you're customizing Claude Code for a single project" or "the configuration is personal and doesn't need to be shared."

**If you wanted this across all your projects**, three options:

1. **User-level skill** (simplest for personal reuse):
   - Create `~/.claude/skills/archive-session/SKILL.md`
   - Same invocation: `/archive-session`
   - Callable from any project
   - But: project-specific Python script path must be flexible (use `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}` in the skill body)

2. **Plugin in skills directory** (versioned, easier to update):
   - Create `~/.claude/skills/my-archive-plugin/plugin.json` + `skills/archive/SKILL.md`
   - Invocation: `/my-archive-plugin:archive`
   - Per [Plugins reference](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/plugins-reference): "plugins in `~/.claude/skills/` load automatically as `name@skills-dir`"
   - Still project-agnostic if the skill uses `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}` to locate project-specific scripts

3. **Distributed plugin** (team/community):
   - Package as separate repo with `plugin.json` manifest
   - Install via `/plugin install &lt;url&gt;`
   - Namespaced: `/my-plugin:archive`

**For now:** `.claude/skills/` in the repo is right. Move to `~/.claude/skills/` only if you find yourself copying the skill to other projects.

## 5. Any other mechanisms?

**No—skill is the right vehicle.** Context:

- **Subagents** (`context: fork`): Overkill for a single sequential workflow; only if you want this to run in isolation from the main conversation
- **Scheduled tasks** (`/schedule`): Wrong trigger (no cron needed; you're typing manually at a specific moment)
- **Monitors**: Not applicable (no background watching needed)
- **MCP servers**: Not applicable (this is local coordination, not external tool integration)

**Summary for your architecture:**

| Choice | Why |
|--------|-----|
| ✓ **Skill** | User-typed, interactive, judgment-driven; bundles Python script; `disable-model-invocation: true` enforces manual timing |
| ✗ Hooks | Headless, non-interactive, automatic—wrong for deliberate end-of-session workflow |
| ✗ Plugin (for now) | Correct distribution wrapper, but only if sharing across projects |
| ✗ Commands | Functionally identical to skill, but skill's directory + frontmatter are cleaner |

**Verdict:** Your SKILL.md approach is idiomatic and well-scoped. Not overkill—it's exactly the right tool for a typed, semi-interactive, project-specific end-of-session workflow.

Verdict from the docs: **a skill was the right call — not overkill.** And there's one small enhancement worth applying. Here's the honest breakdown.

**Skill vs. slash command — they're the same thing now.** In current Claude Code, custom commands (`.claude/commands/*.md`) have been *merged into* skills — both create a `/name` you type, with identical invocation, `$ARGUMENTS`, `!bash`, `@file`, and frontmatter. The skill's *directory* form is actually the cleaner of the two here because it can bundle helper files and carries richer frontmatter. So the thing you asked for is the idiomatic vehicle; there was no "better but overlooked" command form.

**Plugin — not an alternative, a wrapper.** A plugin bundles skills/commands/hooks/MCP for *distribution* (across repos, teams, a marketplace). It'd be the right move only if you wanted this workflow in *all* your projects — but the `finalize-session.py` script and the `development/` convention are project-specific, so committing the skill in this repo is correct for now. (If you later find yourself copying it around, the path is a user-level `~/.claude/skills/` version that locates the per-project script via `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}`, or a plugin — but don't reach for that until you actually have the second project.)

**Hook — deliberately the wrong fit, and good that we avoided it.** A `SessionEnd`/`Stop` hook would run *automatically* and *headless*: no `/dev/tty`, no way to ask you to paste `/usage`, no judgment for the folder/slug. You explicitly want to *decide the moment and type it* — that's precisely what hooks can't do and skills can.

Nothing else (subagents, scheduled tasks, monitors, MCP) fits a typed, semi-interactive, end-of-session workflow better.

## Assistant

Before you run it — one important gotcha, then the answer on reloading.

**The critical thing: don't restart into a fresh session to pick up the skill.** `finalize-session.py` defaults to the *newest* JSONL under `~/.claude/projects/-workspace/`. Right now that newest file **is this session** — which is what you want to archive. If you quit and start a new Claude Code session to register the skill, that new (near-empty) session becomes the newest JSONL, and the skill would archive *it* instead of this one.

This session's JSONL, for reference / pinning:
`/home/node/.claude/projects/-workspace/a6179f1a-c0e2-471f-afe6-f142e43092b9.jsonl`

**On reloading:** the skill was created *during* this session, so it wasn't in the skill list the session loaded at startup — there's a real chance `/archive-session` isn't registered in this running process yet. I can't confirm whether your build hot-scans `.claude/skills/`; the quick test is just to type it. Two cases:

1. **`/archive-session` is recognized** → great. It'll run in this session, so "newest JSONL" correctly points here. Go ahead and type it (optionally `/archive-session 2026-07-03-archive-session` to name the folder explicitly). I'll then follow the skill: run `rtk gain`, call ctx-stats, ask you to paste `/usage`, run the script, and scaffold `analytics.md`.

2. **It's *not* recognized** → tell me. Rather than restart (which breaks the JSONL default), I'll run the exact steps the skill defines, **pinned to this session's JSONL with `--jsonl`**, so you still get a correct archive to review. Same script, same output — just invoked by me instead of via `/`.

A couple of notes:
- I added `disable-model-invocation: true`, so I *won't* auto-fire it — it's yours to type. That flag doesn't block you typing `/archive-session`; it only stops me from triggering it on my own.
- No PROMPT.md in the folder is fine — prompts are optional inputs. If you want this meta-session's original prompt in the record, drop it in as `01-*.prompt.md` before we commit; otherwise the transcript + statistics stand on their own.

## Assistant

Starting with the in-session captures (rtk gain to a file) and loading the ctx-stats tool.

### ⚙ Tool call: `Bash`

```json
{
  "command": "cd /workspace\nDIR=development/2026-07-03-archive-session\nif command -v rtk >/dev/null 2>&1; then\n  rtk gain | tee \"$DIR/rtk.raw.txt\"\nelse\n  echo \"rtk not on PATH — skipping rtk capture\"\nfi",
  "description": "Capture rtk gain output to rtk.raw.txt"
}
```

## Assistant

The finalizer ran and produced everything, but the scrub check flagged a line — let me show you it's a **false positive, not a leak**, and pull up the statistics. That grep matched the literal word "SMTP_PASSWORD" inside *my own exploration prompt* ("where do SMTP_PASSWORD, machine tokens, AWS keys come from") — a prose mention of the name, not a credential value. The scrub regex only redacts `KEY=value` forms, so it correctly left the prose alone. Let me verify precisely and show the stats.

### ⚙ Tool call: `Bash`

```json
{
  "command": "cd /workspace\nDIR=development/2026-07-03-archive-session\necho \"=== REAL secret-VALUE checks (assignments / key shapes / tokens) — expect 0 ===\"\necho -n \"KEY=value or KEY: value assignments: \"\ngrep -cE '(SMTP_PASSWORD|AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID|AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY|CLOUDFLARE_API_KEY)[[:space:]]*[=:][[:space:]]*[^[:space:]«]' \"$DIR/transcript.md\"\necho -n \"AKIA key IDs: \"; grep -coE 'AKIA[0-9A-Z]{16}' \"$DIR/transcript.md\"\necho -n \"PEM private keys: \"; grep -c 'BEGIN [A-Z ]*PRIVATE KEY' \"$DIR/transcript.md\"\necho -n \"Bearer <token> with real value: \"; grep -coE 'Bearer [A-Za-z0-9._-]{12,}' \"$DIR/transcript.md\"\necho -n \"REDACTED markers present (proof scrubber ran where needed): \"; grep -coE '«REDACTED' \"$DIR/transcript.md\"\necho\necho \"=== what the broad grep actually matched (prose mentions) ===\"\ngrep -noE '.{0,15}(SMTP_PASSWORD|Bearer ).{0,15}' \"$DIR/transcript.md\" | head -5\necho\necho \"=== statistics.md ===\"\ncat \"$DIR/statistics.md\"",
  "description": "Precise secret-value checks + show statistics.md"
}
```

## Assistant

That's the whole point of a real trial — it caught a genuine scrubber gap. Here's the honest read:

**No real secret leaked.** Every surviving token is *fake test data* I planted in an earlier scrub self-test this session — `hunter2secret`, `deadbeef…`, AWS's own public example key (which *was* redacted). No real credential from this repo ever entered the session.

**But the test exposed a real bug in the scrubber.** The one assignment-shaped survivor — `CLOUDFLARE_API_KEY: «REDACTED:CLOUDFLARE_API_KEY» — should have been redacted. Cause: my regex required a word boundary (`\b`) *before* the key name, but when a secret sits right after a JSON-escaped newline (`\nCLOUDFLARE_API_KEY=«REDACTED:CLOUDFLARE_API_KEY» which is how command inputs render), the literal `n` glues to the key and defeats `\b`. That's exactly the kind of gap that could bite a real multi-line command. Let me fix it and re-run.

### ⚙ Tool call: `Edit`

```json
{
  "replace_all": false,
  "file_path": "/workspace/development/finalize-session.py",
  "old_string": "    # KEY=value / KEY: value for the known secret env vars\n    (r\"(?i)\\b(SMTP_PASSWORD|AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID|AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY|\"\n     r\"CLOUDFLARE_API_KEY|CLOUDFLARE_EMAIL|ANTHROPIC_API_KEY)\\b(\\s*[=:]\\s*)(\\S+)\",\n     lambda m: m.group(1) + m.group(2) + _REDACT.format(m.group(1))),",
  "new_string": "    # KEY=value / KEY: value for the known secret env vars.  No leading \\b: a\n    # secret rendered right after an escaped newline (\\nKEY=... in a JSON-encoded\n    # command input) glues an `n` before the key and would defeat \\b.\n    (r\"(?i)(SMTP_PASSWORD|AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID|AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY|\"\n     r\"CLOUDFLARE_API_KEY|CLOUDFLARE_EMAIL|ANTHROPIC_API_KEY)(\\s*[=:]\\s*)(\\S+)\",\n     lambda m: m.group(1) + m.group(2) + _REDACT.format(m.group(1))),"
}
```

### ↳ Tool result

```
The file /workspace/development/finalize-session.py has been updated successfully. (file state is current in your context — no need to Read it back)
```

They're bare quoted words, not `KEY=value` secrets, so the value-shaped scrubber correctly leaves them (redacting arbitrary quoted words would mangle legitimate content). Two real takeaways:

1. A normal feature session wouldn't contain fake `SMTP_PASSWORD=«REDACTED:SMTP_PASSWORD» fixtures — this meta-session is a worst case for the "bare mentions" metric.

## Assistant

Cost is in and the value-shaped secret check is **clean**. But re-running surfaced one more real discrepancy I won't sweep under the rug: the JSONL-derived **Token usage** table (opus: 60k in / 448k out) doesn't match `/usage` (48.5k in / 160.4k out). That's a ~2.8× overcount on output — the committed stats file shouldn't contradict itself. Let me diagnose the cause before we commit.

### ⚙ Tool call: `mcp__plugin_context-mode_context-mode__ctx_execute`

```json
{
  "language": "python",
  "code": "\nimport json\np=\"/home/node/.claude/projects/-workspace/a6179f1a-c0e2-471f-afe6-f142e43092b9.jsonl\"\nrows=[json.loads(l) for l in open(p) if l.strip()]\nfrom collections import Counter\nmain=dict(inp=0,out=0,n=0); side=dict(inp=0,out=0,n=0)\nmodels_main=Counter(); models_side=Counter()\nfor r in rows:\n    if r.get(\"type\")!=\"assistant\": continue\n    m=r.get(\"message\") or {}\n    u=m.get(\"usage\") or {}\n    d = side if r.get(\"isSidechain\") else main\n    d[\"inp\"]+=u.get(\"input_tokens\",0); d[\"out\"]+=u.get(\"output_tokens\",0); d[\"n\"]+=1\n    (models_side if r.get(\"isSidechain\") else models_main)[m.get(\"model\")]+=1\nprint(\"MAIN chain :\", main, dict(models_main))\nprint(\"SIDE chain :\", side, dict(models_side))\nprint(\"combined out:\", main[\"out\"]+side[\"out\"])\nprint(\"/usage said : opus 48.5k in / 160.4k out ; haiku 101.5k in / 12.3k out\")\n"

import json
p="/home/node/.claude/projects/-workspace/a6179f1a-c0e2-471f-afe6-f142e43092b9.jsonl"

from collections import Counter
main=dict(inp=0,out=0,n=0); side=dict(inp=0,out=0,n=0)
models_main=Counter(); models_side=Counter()
for r in rows:
    if r.get("type")!="assistant": continue
    m=r.get("message") or {}
    u=m.get("usage") or {}
    d = side if r.get("isSidechain") else main
    d["inp"]+=u.get("input_tokens",0); d["out"]+=u.get("output_tokens",0); d["n"]+=1

## Assistant

Not sidechains (subagents write to their own JSONL files). It's 174 assistant *entries* summing to 457k output, but `/usage` says 160k — so multiple JSONL rows are carrying overlapping/duplicate `usage` for the same underlying API request. The likely dedupe key is `requestId`. Let me test that theory before deciding.

### ⚙ Tool call: `mcp__plugin_context-mode_context-mode__ctx_execute`

```json
{
  "language": "python",
  "code": "\nimport json\np=\"/home/node/.claude/projects/-workspace/a6179f1a-c0e2-471f-afe6-f142e43092b9.jsonl\"\nrows=[json.loads(l) for l in open(p) if l.strip()]\n\n# naive: sum every assistant message's usage\nnaive=dict(inp=0,out=0,cr=0,cw=0,n=0)\n# dedupe: one usage per unique requestId (keep the max, in case of partial then final)\nby_req={}\nno_req=0\nfor r in rows:\n    if r.get(\"type\")!=\"assistant\": continue\n    m=r.get(\"message\") or {}; naive[\"n\"]+=1\n    rid=r.get(\"requestId\")\n    if rid is None: no_req+=1\n    key=rid if rid is not None else (\"_msgid\", m.get(\"id\"))\n    # keep the row with the largest output_tokens for this request/message id\n    prev=by_req.get(key)\n    if prev is None or u.get(\"output_tokens\",0)>prev.get(\"output_tokens\",0):\n        by_req[key]=u\n\nded=dict(inp=0,out=0,cr=0,cw=0)\nfor u in by_req.values():\n    ded[\"inp\"]+=u.get(\"input_tokens\",0); ```
```python

import json
p="/home/node/.claude/projects/-workspace/a6179f1a-c0e2-471f-afe6-f142e43092b9.jsonl"
rows=[json.loads(l) for l in open(p) if l.strip()]

# naive: sum every assistant message's usage
naive=dict(inp=0,out=0,cr=0,cw=0,n=0)
# dedupe: one usage per unique requestId (keep the max, in case of partial then final)
by_req={}
no_req=0
for r in rows:
    if r.get("type")!="assistant": continue
    m=r.get("message") or {}; u=m.get("usage") or {}
    naive["inp"]+=u.get("input_tokens",0); naive["out"]+=u.get("output_tokens",0)
    naive["cr"]+=u.get("cache_read_input_tokens",0); naive["cw"]+=u.get("cache_creation_input_tokens",0); naive["n"]+=1
    rid=r.get("requestId")
    if rid is None: no_req+=1
    key=rid if rid is not None else ("_msgid", m.get("id"))
    # keep the row with the largest output_tokens for this request/message id
    prev=by_req.get(key)
    if prev is None or u.get("output_tokens",0)>prev.get("output_tokens",0):
        by_req[key]=u

ded=dict(inp=0,out=0,cr=0,cw=0)
for u in by_req.values():
    ded["inp"]+=u.get("input_tokens",0); ded["out"]+=u.get("output_tokens",0)
    ded["cr"]+=u.get("cache_read_input_tokens",0); ded["cw"]+=u.get("cache_creation_input_tokens",0)

print("assistant entries:", naive["n"], "| unique requestIds+msgfallback:", len(by_req), "| rows w/o requestId:", no_req)
print("NAIVE  in/out/cr/cw:", naive["inp"], naive["out"], naive["cr"], naive["cw"])
print("DEDUP  in/out/cr/cw:", ded["inp"], ded["out"], ded["cr"], ded["cw"])
print("/usage opus        : 48500 / 160400 / 17300000 / 1000000  (approx, from display)")

# also: how many distinct message.id vs requestId
mids=set(); rids=set()
for r in rows:
    if r.get("type")!="assistant": continue
    rids.add(r.get("requestId")); mids.add((r.get("message") or {}).get("id"))
print("distinct message.id:", len(mids), "distinct requestId:", len(rids))

```

## Assistant

That's the real structure: **63 actual model requests, but 174 JSONL rows** — Claude Code writes multiple rows per assistant message (same `message.id`/`requestId`), and each row repeats the `usage`. Naive summing counts each request ~2.8×. Deduping by `requestId` lands in the right ballpark (140k vs `/usage` 160k — not exact, because the JSONL is internal/approximate, which is exactly why we embed `/usage` as the source of truth).

But this raises a bigger question I need to check: if rows repeat per message, is the **transcript** (and the tool-call counts) also duplicating content? Let me look at how content is split across those rows.

### ⚙ Tool call: `mcp__plugin_context-mode_context-mode__ctx_execute`

```json
{
  "language": "python",
  "code": "\nimport json\nfrom collections import defaultdict, Counter\np=\"/home/node/.claude/projects/-workspace/a6179f1a-c0e2-471f-afe6-f142e43092b9.jsonl\"\nrows=[json.loads(l) for l in open(p) if l.strip()]\n\nby_id=defaultdict(list)\nfor r in rows:\n    if r.get(\"type\")==\"assistant\":\n        by_id[(r.get(\"message\") or {}).get(\"id\")].append(r)\n\n# pick a message.id that has multiple rows; ### ↳ Tool result

```
```python

import json
from collections import defaultdict, Counter
p="/home/node/.claude/projects/-workspace/a6179f1a-c0e2-471f-afe6-f142e43092b9.jsonl"
rows=[json.loads(l) for l in open(p) if l.strip()]

by_id=defaultdict(list)
for r in rows:
    if r.get("type")=="assistant":
        by_id[(r.get("message") or {}).get("id")].append(r)

# pick a message.id that has multiple rows; show block types per row
multi=[(mid,rs) for mid,rs in by_id.items() if len(rs)>1]
print("assistant message.ids:", len(by_id), "| with >1 row:", len(multi))
mid,rs=max(multi,key=lambda kv:len(kv[1]))
print(f"\nexample message.id with {len(rs)} rows — block types per row:")
for i,r in enumerate(rs):
    c=(r.get("message") or {}).get("content")
    bt=[b.get("type") for b in c] if isinstance(c,list) else [type(c).__name__]
    print(f"  row {i}: {bt}")

# tool_use dedupe check: naive count vs unique toolu ids
naive_tools=Counter(); ids=set(); uniq_tools=Counter()
for r in rows:
    if r.get("type")!="assistant": continue
    for b in ((r.get("message") or {}).get("content") or []):
        if isinstance(b,dict) and b.get("type")=="tool_use":
            naive_tools[b.get("name")]+=1
            if b.get("id") not in ids:
                ids.add(b.get("id")); uniq_tools[b.get("name")]+=1
print("\ntool_use blocks — naive total:", sum(naive_tools.values()), "| unique by id:", sum(uniq_tools.values()))
print("naive:", dict(naive_tools))
print("uniq :", dict(uniq_tools))

# text block dup check: do multiple rows of same id repeat identical text?
dupe_text=0; total_text=0
for mid,rs in by_id.items():
    seen=set()
    for r in rs:
        for b in ((r.get("message") or {}).get("content") or []):
            if isinstance(b,dict) and b.get("type")=="text":
                total_text+=1
                t=b.get("text","")
                if t in seen: dupe_text+=1
                seen.add(t)
print("\ntext blocks total:", total_text, "| duplicated within same message.id:", dupe_text)

uniq : {'Agent': 2, 'AskUserQuestion': 7, 'Write': 10, 'ToolSearch': 5, 'ExitPlanMode': 4, 'Edit': 21, 'mcp__plugin_context-mode_context-mode__ctx_execute': 5, 'Skill': 1, 'TaskCreate': 5, 'Bash': 12, 'TaskUpdate': 5, 'Read': 2, 'SendMessage': 1, 'mcp__plugin_context-mode_context-mode__ctx_stats': 1}

## Assistant

Now it's fully diagnosed, and the news is mostly good:

- **Transcript is correct** — content is *not* duplicated (each row carries one distinct block; 0 duplicated text blocks). The rendered transcript is faithful.
- **Tool-call counts are correct** — 81 naive == 81 unique-by-id, no inflation.
- **Only two things were wrong, both from counting rows instead of requests:** the token sums (usage repeated on every row → 2.8× over) and "Assistant turns" (174 rows vs 64 real turns).

So the fix is contained: dedupe usage per request, and count turns by request. Even deduped, JSONL tokens won't perfectly equal `/usage` (internal format), so I'll keep `/usage` as the labeled authority. Applying it.

### ⚙ Tool call: `Edit`

```json
{
  "replace_all": false,
  "file_path": "/workspace/development/finalize-session.py",
  "old_string": "def collect_stats(rows):\n    per_model = {}   # model -> token sums\n    tools = {}       # tool name -> count\n    turns = 0\n    max_ctx = 0\n    first = last = None\n    for row in rows:\n        ts = _ts(row)\n        if ts:\n            first = first or ts\n            last = ts\n        if row.get(\"type\") != \"assistant\":\n            continue\n        msg = row.get(\"message\")\n        if not isinstance(msg, dict):\n            continue\n        turns += 1\n        model = msg.get(\"model\", \"unknown\")\n        u = msg.get(\"usage\") or {}\n        creation = u.get(\"cache_creation\") or {}\n        acc = per_model.setdefault(model, dict(inp=0, out=0, read=0, w5=0, w1=0))\n        acc[\"inp\"] += u.get(\"input_tokens\", 0)\n        acc[\"out\"] += u.get(\"output_tokens\", 0)\n        acc[\"read\"] += u.get(\"cache_read_input_tokens\", 0)\n        acc[\"w5\"] += creation.get(\"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens\", 0)\n        acc[\"w1\"] += creation.get(\"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens\", 0)\n        # Context approximation: the largest single prompt sent this session.\n        prompt = (u.get(\"input_tokens\", 0) + u.get(\"cache_read_input_tokens\", 0)\n                  + u.get(\"cache_creation_input_tokens\", 0))\n        max_ctx = max(max_ctx, prompt)\n        for b in _blocks(msg):\n            if isinstance(b, dict) and b.get(\"type\") == \"tool_use\":\n                tools[b.get(\"name\", \"?\")] = tools.get(b.get(\"name\", \"?\"), 0) + 1\n    return dict(per_model=per_model, tools=tools, turns=turns,\n                max_ctx=max_ctx, first=first, last=last)",
  "new_string": "def collect_stats(rows):\n    # Claude Code writes ONE JSONL row per content block, so a single assistant\n    # request spans several rows that all repeat the same `usage` block.  Summing\n    # per-row would multiply tokens (~3x here) and turns.  So: dedupe usage per\n    # request (keyed by requestId, falling back to message.id), but count tool_use\n    # blocks per unique block id (each block appears on exactly one row).\n    per_model = {}\n    tools = {}\n    seen_tool_ids = set()\n    req_usage = {}   # request key -> (model, usage) — keep the row with max output\n    first = last = None\n    for row in rows:\n        ts = _ts(row)\n        if ts:\n            first = first or ts\n            last = ts\n        if row.get(\"type\") != \"assistant\":\n            continue\n        msg = row.get(\"message\")\n        if not isinstance(msg, dict):\n            continue\n        key = row.get(\"requestId\") or msg.get(\"id\") or id(row)\n        u = msg.get(\"usage\") or {}\n        prev = req_usage.get(key)\n        if prev is None or u.get(\"output_tokens\", 0) > prev[1].get(\"output_tokens\", 0):\n            req_usage[key] = (msg.get(\"model\", \"unknown\"), u)\n        for b in _blocks(msg):\n            if isinstance(b, dict) and b.get(\"type\") == \"tool_use\":\n                tid = b.get(\"id\")\n                if tid in seen_tool_ids:\n                    continue\n                seen_tool_ids.add(tid)\n                tools[b.get(\"name\", \"?\")] = tools.get(b.get(\"name\", \"?\"), 0) + 1\n\n    max_ctx = 0\n    for model, u in req_usage.values():\n        creation = u.get(\"cache_creation\") or {}\n        acc = per_model.setdefault(model, dict(inp=0, out=0, read=0, w5=0, w1=0))\n        acc[\"inp\"] += u.get(\"input_tokens\", 0)\n        acc[\"out\"] += u.get(\"output_tokens\", 0)\n        acc[\"read\"] += u.get(\"cache_read_input_tokens\", 0)\n        acc[\"w5\"] += creation.get(\"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens\", 0)\n        acc[\"w1\"] += creation.get(\"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens\", 0)\n        # Context approximation: the largest single prompt sent this session.\n        prompt = (u.get(\"input_tokens\", 0) + u.get(\"cache_read_input_tokens\", 0)\n                  + u.get(\"cache_creation_input_tokens\", 0))\n        max_ctx = max(max_ctx, prompt)\n\n    return dict(per_model=per_model, tools=tools, turns=len(req_usage),\n                max_ctx=max_ctx, first=first, last=last)"
}
